class="stElementContainer element-container st-emotion-cache-kj6hex eu6p4el1" data-testid="stElementContainer" data-stale="false" width="auto"><div class="stMarkdown" data-testid="stMarkdown"><div data-testid="stMarkdownContainer" class="st-emotion-cache-1104ytp e1icttdg0"><p>UNIT THREE PART TWO: ABNORMAL LABOUR AND PUERPERIUM</p>
<p>In part two of this unit you will focus on some of the common problems that occur due to abnormalities in labour, such as; multiple pregnancies, common abnormal presentations including breech and shoulder presentation and positions including the occipito-posterior. You shall look at how these conditions present and your role as a midwife in preventing the problem from getting worse.</p>
<p>This unit is composed of five sections:</p>
<p>Section One: Multiple Pregnancies
Section Two: Abnormal Uterine Action
Section Three: Trial of Labour, Induction of Labour and Prolonged Labour
Section Four: Abnormal Puerperium
Section Five: Obstetric Anaesthesia Operations and Emergencies
Unit Objectives</p>
<p>By the end of part two you will be able to:</p>
<ul>
<li>Describe the management of multiple pregnancy</li>
<li>Describe the management of abnormal uterine action</li>
<li>Explain the process of managing trial of labour</li>
<li>Describe the management of foetal malpositions</li>
<li>Describe the management of foetal malpresentations</li>
<li>Explain the management of puerperal sepsis</li>
<li>Describe the management of breast complications</li>
<li>Explain how to manage mental health conditions related to pregnancy and childbirth</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="section-1-multiple-pregnancies">SECTION 1: MULTIPLE PREGNANCIES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#section-1-multiple-pregnancies" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="introduction">Introduction<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#introduction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Multiple pregnancy is a term applied when there is more than one foetus in the uterus. The incidence of multiple pregnancies is rare. It is estimated that twin conception occurs spontaneously once in 90 pregnancies, triplets once in 310,000 while quadruplets occur once in 700,000.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="objectives">Objectives<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#objectives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>By the end of this section you will be able to:</p>
<ul>
<li>Define multiple pregnancy</li>
<li>Explain the two different types of twins</li>
<li>Diagnose twin pregnancy</li>
<li>Describe the effect of multiple pregnancy on pregnancy</li>
<li>Describe the management of multiple pregnancies</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="multiple-pregnancies">Multiple Pregnancies<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#multiple-pregnancies" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="varieties-of-twins">Varieties of Twins<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#varieties-of-twins" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Twins may be binovular or uniovular. Binovular twins are developed from two separate ova, which may or may not come from the same ovary. Uniovular twins are developed from a single fertilised ovum, which undergoes division to form two embryos.</p>
<p>Below is a comparison of the two types of twins.</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Uniovular twin (monozygotic)</th><th>Binovular twins (dizygotic)</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>One ovum</td><td>Two ova</td></tr><tr><td>One spermatozoon</td><td>Two spermatozoa</td></tr><tr><td>One amnion</td><td>Two amnions</td></tr><tr><td>One chorion</td><td>Two chorions</td></tr><tr><td>One placenta</td><td>Two placentas (may fuse)</td></tr><tr><td>Same sex</td><td>Same or different sexes</td></tr><tr><td>Identical</td><td>May be different in appearance</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 153 of 317
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 154 of 317
Bishop's Computers</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="diagnosing-a-multiple-pregnancy">Diagnosing a Multiple Pregnancy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnosing-a-multiple-pregnancy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="on-inspection">On Inspection<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#on-inspection" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>The abdomen looks larger than it should at the given date</li>
<li>Polyhydramnios may increase the abdominal size leading to confusion of the diagnosis</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="on-palpation">On Palpation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#on-palpation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Abdominal girth will be 101.5 or more centimetres</li>
<li>Fundal height is larger than dates from twentieth week of gestation</li>
<li>You will reveal two foetal poles on fundal palpation</li>
<li>The size of the head is smaller than the size of the uterus</li>
<li>You will palpate an unusual number of foetal parts</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="on-auscultation">On Auscultation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#on-auscultation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Two foetal hearts are recorded simultaneously and there is a difference of 10 to 20 beats</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="ultrasound-scan">Ultrasound Scan<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ultrasound-scan" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>An ultrasound scan at seventh week can distinguish two separate sacs while from the twelfth week two foetal bodies can be identified. On the fourteenth week, two heads can be detected.</p>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> Two skeletons are visible on x-ray at thirty weeks.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="effects-of-multiple-pregnancy">Effects of Multiple Pregnancy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#effects-of-multiple-pregnancy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The effects of twins on pregnancy include:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Preeclampsia is three times more common in multiple pregnancies than a single pregnancy</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Anaemia is more common, due to the increased foetal demand of folic acid and iron dietary requirement</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Polyhydramnios could occur due to more fluid in the two foetal sacs</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Pressure symptoms are more marked, and may include backache, oedema, varicose veins, indigestion, constipation, dyspnoea and bladder irritability</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Minor disorders of pregnancy are more marked, including headache, morning sickness and vomiting</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Premature labour is likely, due to over stretching of the uterus</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Congenital malformation occurs twice as much than in single pregnancy</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Intrauterine growth retardation may occur due to placenta insufficiency</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Complications of twins in pregnancy include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Malpresentation, where 35% of twins will both present by the head, and another 35% by head and breech. 10% present by breech and/or 20% present by transverse lie or cephalic with transverse lie</li>
<li>Delay in the birth of the second twin</li>
<li>Cord prolapse, which occurs especially with the second twin, often when there is malpresentation</li>
<li>Maternal and foetal distress is common due to prolonged labour</li>
<li>Locked twins is a rare complication but may prevent spontaneous delivery</li>
<li>Postpartum haemorrhage due to large placental site</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="multiple-pregnancy-management">Multiple Pregnancy Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#multiple-pregnancy-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management-during-the-antenatal-period">Management During the Antenatal Period<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-during-the-antenatal-period" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Intensify the care of the mother of twins by ensuring the following:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>See the patient every two weeks from the 20th week</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Check blood haemoglobin levels at 30, 36, 37 weeks before labour to exclude anaemia</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Relieve any discomfort by advising on remedies for minor disorders of pregnancy</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Advise on diet to prevent anaemia</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Advise on the need for at least two hours rest in the afternoon and six to eight hours rest during the night</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The practice of admitting the patient between 30 to 36 weeks is now uncommon. It was necessary where home conditions were poor. It was intended for improving foetal growth through increased placental blood flow following enough rest in the hospital</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Improve maternal nutritional status</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Never allow the pregnancy to go post mature (post date) due to the danger of placenta insufficiency</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management-during-first-stage-of-labour">Management During First Stage of Labour<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-during-first-stage-of-labour" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>All cases of multiple pregnancy should be delivered in hospitals due to complications that may occur during labour. The following procedure should be followed:</p>
<ul>
<li>Take blood for grouping and cross match</li>
<li>Avoid over sedating the mother during labour</li>
<li>Prepare your delivery trolley with pairs of instruments for two babies. You should have a resuscitation trolley, baby labels, ergometrine or syntometrine in a syringe</li>
<li>Put up the oxytocin drip if uterine action is not proving very effective</li>
<li>Monitor and assess the progress of labour</li>
<li>Delivery room must be warm</li>
<li>Time the episiotomy properly</li>
<li>Check foetal heart beats between each contraction</li>
<li>Advise on ambulation if membranes are intact</li>
<li>Encourage the mother to empty her bladder</li>
<li>Reassure the mother</li>
<li>Be friendly and display positive attitudes towards the mother and her family members</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management-during-second-stage-of-labour">Management During Second Stage of Labour<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-during-second-stage-of-labour" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Ensure that the following procedure is followed when managing the second stage of labour:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>It is preferable to have an obstetrician, paediatrician and anaesthetist present during the delivery.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Preparations should be made for resuscitation and special care in case of low birth weight.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Operating theatres should be ready to receive a mother at a short notice in case of emergency caesarean section.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Deliver the head of the first twin slowly, clear the airway and hand the baby to the assistants.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The assistant should label the baby and write 'first twin' or 'twin one'.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The lie of the second twin is checked (if longitudinal), then the presenting part is checked. If high, the presenting part is pushed down by fundal pressure and the membranes are ruptured.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The mother is encouraged to push with each contraction and the baby should be born within 45 minutes.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Oxytocin can be given immediately after delivery of the anterior shoulder of the second twin. It may also be administered after delivery of the placenta.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>As soon as the oxytocin takes effect, the uterus contracts.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Both cords are taken simultaneously. The placenta and membranes will be delivered using control cord traction.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="complications-in-the-delivery-of-twins">Complications in the Delivery of Twins<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#complications-in-the-delivery-of-twins" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="management-of-delayed-twin">Management of Delayed Twin<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-delayed-twin" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Should you be confronted with a case of a delayed twin, the following steps should be taken:</p>
<ul>
<li>Ascertain if the lie is longitudinal.</li>
<li>Assess the contraction and, if poor, ask your assistant to commence syntocinon drip to stimulate contraction.</li>
<li>Encourage the mother to push during contraction.</li>
<li>Vacuum extraction may be done when the doctor comes.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="management-when-second-twin-lies-in-transverse">Management When Second Twin Lies in Transverse<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-when-second-twin-lies-in-transverse" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>You must ensure that you follow this procedure should you be confronted with a case where the second twin is lying in transverse:</p>
<ul>
<li>Send for the doctor.</li>
<li>Attempt external version when the membranes are intact.</li>
<li>If you succeed in performing the external version, rupture the membranes and encourage the mother to push the baby.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Remember:</strong> In case you do not succeed, the doctor will perform an internal version and deliver the baby in breech.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="expulsion-of-the-placenta-or-bleeding-before-second-twin">Expulsion of the Placenta or Bleeding Before Second Twin<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#expulsion-of-the-placenta-or-bleeding-before-second-twin" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>If the placenta is expelled soon after the first twin or there is bleeding:</p>
<ul>
<li>You should deliver the second twin as soon as possible by using fundal pressure in case of longitudinal lie.</li>
</ul>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<ul>
<li>If this is not possible, inform a doctor as soon as possible and prepare the mother for caesarian section.</li>
<li>Locked twins are very rare. To facilitate the birth of the second twin, decapitation of the first twin is necessary, but caesarean section for delivery of the second twin is the easiest and safest method.</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260112-c4adf602.jpeg" alt="img-0.jpeg">
A</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260112-7b8f0f31.jpeg" alt="img-1.jpeg">
B</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="conjoined-twins">Conjoined Twins<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#conjoined-twins" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A case of conjoined twins usually requires a cesarean section. At times separation of the conjoined twins is possible.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="version">Version<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#version" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is turning the foetus from an undesirable position to a desirable position. The two types of version are external version and pondalic (or internal) version.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="external-version">External Version<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#external-version" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is the external manipulation of the foetus through the abdomen and the uterine walls, used to correct malpresentation. The procedure is successful when done a month before term. Unfortunately, it is often felt that the foetus returns to its original position after a few hours. This procedure is outdated as caesarean section is recommended in malpresentations. It is now used by a midwife only in the delivery of the second twin in the case of transverse lie.</p>
<p>External version is contraindicated in the case of antepartum haemorrhage, high blood pressure, rhesus negative mother, previous scars and twin pregnancy.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="preparation">Preparation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#preparation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Reassure the mother by explaining the procedure</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Make sure the bladder is empty</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The mother lies with partial flexion of the thighs to relax her abdominal muscles</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Sprinkle powder on her abdomen to prevent friction during the movement</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Engage the mother in conversation during the procedure to divert her attention so as to be relaxed. (Some doctors order valium one to two hours before the procedure)</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="disengage-breech">Disengage Breech<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#disengage-breech" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The doctor will locate the head and the back and disengage breech by pushing the breech upward with the fingers of both hands. Refer to the diagram on the right.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260112-f1744e6d.jpeg" alt="img-2.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="make-the-foetus-do-a-forward-somersault">Make the Foetus do a Forward Somersault<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#make-the-foetus-do-a-forward-somersault" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Using steady pressure with one hand press upwards, turn the foetus laterally while the other hand presses on the head displacing it in the direction, which will increase flexion. (Follow the foetus' nose otherwise you will extend the head.)</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 156 of 317
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260112-ed0d554c.jpeg" alt="img-3.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="post-version-steps">Post-Version Steps<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#post-version-steps" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Take the foetal heartbeat immediately after the version. For the first few minutes there may be alteration of the heartbeat but it will pick up within a few minutes.</li>
<li>Observe the mother for three hours.</li>
<li>If there is no bleeding per vagina, draining of liquor or contraction, advise the mother to report back after one week unless any problem arises.</li>
<li>If the mother is rhesus negative, anti D should be given within the first 72 hours.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="pondalic-version">Pondalic Version<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pondalic-version" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is a manoeuvre designed to change any existing presentation to breech presentation. It is also known as internal version. This manoeuvre is useful in delivery of delayed or transverse second twin. It is now never used in any other circumstances.</p>
<p>While the cervical os is fully dilated, the whole hand is introduced high in the uterus. The baby's feet are grasped and pulled in the direction of the birth canal. The other hand helps to turn the foetus by pushing the head up at the fundus. The version is followed by breech extraction.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="care-during-puerperium">Care During Puerperium<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#care-during-puerperium" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>For the mother with multiple births, involution is usually slow. The after pain is also often more troublesome. Care of the babies can be a major problem, so the mother should be initially helped with the feeding of the babies. Teach the mother how to feed so that she feels competent when discharged. For more detailed information see the section on Care of Normal Puerperium.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="section-2-abnormal-uterine-action">SECTION 2: ABNORMAL UTERINE ACTION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#section-2-abnormal-uterine-action" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="introduction">Introduction<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#introduction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Before you begin this section, it is recommended that you review the normal uterine function as you learnt it in the physiology of labour. This section explores abnormalities in uterine action, their causes and management.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="objectives">Objectives<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#objectives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>By the end of this section you will be able to:</p>
<ul>
<li>Explain the concept of abnormal uterine action</li>
<li>Analyse the different types of abnormal uterine action</li>
<li>Identify causes of various types of abnormal uterine action</li>
<li>Describe the management of each type of abnormal uterine action</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="abnormal-uterine-action">Abnormal Uterine Action<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#abnormal-uterine-action" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Abnormal uterine action is a dysfunction of uterine muscles due to neuromuscular disharmony. Some types of abnormal uterine action include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Hypotonic uterine action</li>
<li>Incoordinate uterine action, including hypertonic lower uterine segment, constriction ring dystocia, colicky uterus and spurious labour</li>
<li>Cervical dystocia</li>
<li>Precipitate labour</li>
</ul>
<p>You will now explore each of these conditions in more detail.</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260112-cd514d74.jpeg" alt="img-4.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="hypotonic-uterine-action">Hypotonic Uterine Action<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hypotonic-uterine-action" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>This is poor tone in the uterine muscle fibres which results from weak/short contractions. The contractions are infrequent and cause less pain. The uterus may be indented at the height of a contraction. Both mother and baby are affected by the contractions. The effects of weak contractions bring about very slow or no cervical dilatation. This results in prolonged labour.</p>
<p>There are two types of hypotonia; primary and secondary uterine inertia also respectively known as primary and secondary hypotonia. Primary hypotonia starts at the onset of labour. The cause is unknown and it is common in primigravida. Secondary hypotonia occurs when labour has already been established. The uterus is exhausted and contractions slow down, due to:</p>
<ul>
<li>Retained second twin</li>
<li>Cephalopelvic disproportion</li>
<li>Malpresentation or malposition</li>
<li>Effect after epidural anaesthesia</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management-of-hypotonic-uterine-action">Management of Hypotonic Uterine Action<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-hypotonic-uterine-action" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Admit the mother in hospital or transfer to a hospital if she is in a health centre. Reassure her and then sedate her to reduce anxiety and calm her down to sleep. You should perform an abdominal and pelvic exam to exclude cephalopelvic disproportion. Determine the cause of OPP. If this is present she should be prepared for a caesarean section.</p>
<p>If there are no uterine contractions, these should be stimulated by administering an enema or</p>
<p>repeat administration if it had been given previously.</p>
<p>You should check on the following factors:</p>
<ul>
<li>Frequency, strength and duration of the contractions</li>
<li>Vital signs, that is, maternal pulse and BP and general condition</li>
<li>Foetal heart rates</li>
<li>Descent of the presenting part</li>
</ul>
<p>A vaginal examination is done every two to four hours to determine cervical dilatation. The urine is tested every two hours for sugar, acetone and albumin. If there is foetal or maternal distress in the first stage of labour, the mother is prepared for caesarean section. However, if the mother is in the second stage or nearing second stage and contracting and dilating well, the delivery can be assisted by vacuum extraction.</p>
<p>The possibility of post partum haemorrhage should be kept in mind. Hence an intramuscular injection of syntometrin 1ml should be given at the birth of the anterior shoulder or egometrin at the crowning of the head.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="incoordinate-uterine-action">Incoordinate Uterine Action<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#incoordinate-uterine-action" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>In cases of incoordinate uterine action, there is alteration in the polarity of the uterus with an increase in the resting tone. The uterus is very irritable. The contractions are strong, painful and erratic but in spite of strong contractions, the cervix dilates slowly. Clinically, the patient experiences a lot of pain both before and after contraction. She is exhausted and bears down early due to severe backache. This may lead to retention of urine. Foetal hypoxia occurs due to the hypertonic state of uterus, which interferes with the placental circulation.</p>
<p>On Vaginal Examination (VE) the cervix is noted to dilate slowly despite frequent painful contractions. The cervix is tight, unyielding and oedematous since the mother bears down with each contraction. There are four varieties of Incoordinate uterine action, which will be explored on the next page.</p>
<p>There are four varieties of Incoordinate uterine action described below.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="hypertonic-lower-uterine-segment">Hypertonic Lower Uterine Segment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hypertonic-lower-uterine-segment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>In this case, the lower uterine segment is hypertonic. There is loss of polarity and intermittent abdominal pains. The pains occur before and persist long after a uterine contraction. The cervix fails to dilate.</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 159 of 317
Bishop's Computers</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="colicky-uterus">Colicky Uterus<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#colicky-uterus" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The upper uterine segment contracts strongly and spasmodically. As a result of the different parts of the uterus contracting differently the cervical dilatation is ineffective. There may be reduced placental blood flow leading to foetal distress.</p>
<p>There is intense clump-like pain, contractions are not effective and the uterus is tender. The mother may not experience severe backache.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="constriction-ring-dystocia">Constriction Ring Dystocia<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#constriction-ring-dystocia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>This condition happens one in every thousand labours (Myles, 1999). It is a localised spasm of a ring of muscle fibres. This is a result of disorganised uterine action. It is commonly found near the junction of both the upper and lower uterine segment. It usually embraces a narrow part of the neck of the foetus. It may happen at any stage of labour but if it occurs in the third stage, it is known as an hourglass constriction.</p>
<p>The spasm may be triggered by an early rupture of membranes. The hypertonic uterus is irritated by being moulded round the foetus or by interuterine manipulation.</p>
<p>The condition can be diagnosed vaginally when there is a delay in labour. There is no advance of the presenting part and the upper segment feels tender to the touch. Inhalation of amylnitrate or 10ml of 2% IV magnesium sulphate solution may relieve spasms.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="spurious-labour">Spurious Labour<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#spurious-labour" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Spurious labour is a condition where contractions occur before the onset of labour, which are painful and are accompanied by backache. Giving pethidine or morphine 1ml to relax the uterine contractions can abolish them. This differentiates it with true labour.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management-of-incoordinate-uterine-action">Management of Incoordinate Uterine Action<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-incoordinate-uterine-action" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Cephalopelvic Disproportion (CPD) is usually the underlying cause of this condition. Malpresentation should be ruled out through an abdominal and vaginal examination. If malpresentation is present, the patient should be prepared for a caesarean section. If CPD is not present, she may be allowed to continue in labour. Close observation is carried out and a record of observations should be maintained.</p>
<p>Reassure the mother to allay anxiety. Make observations of the foetal heart rate, maternal pulse, and respiratory rate half-hourly. Blood pressure should be taken every four hours and urine testing should be done every two hours. Any signs of maternal/foetal distress; dehydration and ketosis, should be reported promptly and may be corrected by giving intravenously (IV) 5% dextrose alternating with normal saline. You should always maintain an intake and output record.</p>
<p>Sedate the mother to relieve pain, calm her down and enable her to sleep. Epidural analgesia is very effective in prompting normal uterine action (or pethidine if added to the drip). A low dose of 0.5mg syntocinon drip can be given. If, after four to six hours, there is still no progress, the mother should be prepared for a caesarean section.</p>
<p>A small proportion of mothers with Incoordinate uterine action may end up in normal delivery or vacuum extraction. The midwife should be able to make the correct judgement call.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cervical-dystocia">Cervical Dystocia<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cervical-dystocia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Cervical dystocia can be divided into two classes; primary and secondary.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="primary-cervical-dystocia">Primary Cervical Dystocia<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#primary-cervical-dystocia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>In primary cervical dystocia, the uterine contractions are normal. The presenting part is low down in the pelvis but the cervix fails to dilate. The delay is due to the formation of a cartilaginous ring round the cervix.</p>
<p>This condition occurs mainly in primagravida whereby the first stage is prolonged and there is severe and persistent backache. On vaginal examination the cervix feels thin, tight and unyielding.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="secondary-cervical-dystocia">Secondary Cervical Dystocia<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#secondary-cervical-dystocia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>This type occurs due to previous trauma to the cervix, for example, tears which were repaired, scarring or from infection. The cervix fails to dilate in spite of good uterine contractions.</p>
<p>The management of cervical dystocia is by encouraging the mother to lie on her back, elevation of the bed foot to ease pressure on the cervix and care must be taken to avoid lacerations. Caesarean section should be done to hasten delivery of the baby.</p>
<p>Cervical dystocia can be further divided into one of three types, any of which can occur as primary or secondary cervical distocia.</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 160 of 317
Bishop's Computers</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="rigid-cervix">Rigid cervix<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#rigid-cervix" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Rigid cervix is a rare condition in which the cervix fails to dilate despite normal uterine contractions. It is characterised by severe persistent backache. On vaginal examination the cervix feels thin, tight and unyielding.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="annular-detachment-of-the-cervix">Annular detachment of the cervix<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#annular-detachment-of-the-cervix" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Annular detachment of the cervix is characterised by persistent and prolonged pressure on the rigid cervix, which causes ischemia. The necrosed ring of the cervix is detached and expelled and contributes to a uterine rupture.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="oedematous-anterior-lip-of-cervix">Oedematous anterior lip of cervix<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#oedematous-anterior-lip-of-cervix" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Oedematous anterior lip of the cervix involves the anterior lip being nipped between the foetal head and the pelvic brim. It becomes swollen due to pressure. On vaginal examination the oedematous cervix feels like a firm ridge as thick as a finger. It may also be seen at the vulva as a bluish glistering cervix. It delays the first stage of labour, as the cervix does not dilate quickly.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="precipitate-labour">Precipitate Labour<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#precipitate-labour" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>In the case of precipitate labour, the contractions are strong and frequent from the onset of labour. This results in an abnormally rapid progress of labour and delivery may occur within an hour from the onset of labour.</p>
<p>There are several types of complications, which can occur.</p>
<p>Maternal complications include cervical and perenial lacerations. The uterus may fail to contract during the third stage of labour, leading to a retained placenta. Post partum haemorrhage, uterine inversion, shock and collapse may occur due to sudden relief of pressure.</p>
<p>Foetal complications include foetal hypoxia, which may occur as a result of frequent and strong contractions. Rapid moulding may result in intracranial pressure and, during delivery, this may lead to intracranial haemorrhage. Asphyxia may occur due to rapid expulsion of the baby's unmoulded head.</p>
<p>Remember: Precipitate labour tends to recur. Therefore, with future pregnancies the mother needs to be admitted early into hospital for safe delivery.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="over-stimulation-of-the-uterus">Over-Stimulation of the Uterus<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#over-stimulation-of-the-uterus" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>This may occur as a result of excessive use of syntocinon or prostaglandin, which may cause tetanic contractions with inadequate periods of relaxation.</p>
<p>Complications of over-stimulation of the uterus include foetal hypoxia. If uterine spasms that reduce the transfer from the placenta of foetal oxygen are not treated, foetal death may occur. Other complications include precipitate labour and rupture of uterus in cases of disproportion.</p>
<p>Methods of management should include the following:</p>
<ul>
<li>Stop the administration of syntocinon or prostaglandin at once</li>
<li>In case of tonic contractions, the patient should be given two puffs of ventolin inhaler</li>
<li>If there is foetal distress, give dextrose IV and oxygen by mask</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="tonic-contractions">Tonic Contractions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#tonic-contractions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>This is where the contractions are excessively longer, stronger and more frequent. This results in almost continuous contractions with short periods of relaxation. Tonic contractions are caused by cephalopelvic disproportion. The uterus attempts to overcome the obstruction and so it increases its strength and frequency. The condition is common in primigravidae.</p>
<p>Possible complications of tonic contractions include the rupture of the uterus and foetal death due to prolonged labour.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management-of-tonic-contractions">Management of Tonic Contractions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-tonic-contractions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>If the patient is on syntocinon drip, it should be discontinued and the doctor informed. The vital signs, including observations of pulse and blood pressure, should be monitored carefully.</p>
<p>There are several factors, which predispose to abnormal uterine action, these include:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Age, the elderly primigravida is more likely to have abnormal uterine action</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Parity, the condition is more frequent in primigravida</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Cephalopelvic disproportion or malpresentation OPP, which may either cause hypotonic uterine action or incoordinate uterine action</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Post maturity</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Other factors like over distension of the uterus in multiple pregnancy</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Early rupture of membranes</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Emotional tension of the patient</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="section-3-trial-of-labour-induction-of-labour-and-prolonged-labour">SECTION 3: TRIAL OF LABOUR, INDUCTION OF LABOUR AND PROLONGED LABOUR<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#section-3-trial-of-labour-induction-of-labour-and-prolonged-labour" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="introduction">Introduction<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#introduction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This section examines difficulties that can be experienced during labour, how labour can be induced and the conditions of prolonged and obstructed labour.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="objectives">Objectives<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#objectives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>By the end of this section you will be able to:</p>
<ul>
<li>Define trial of vaginal delivery</li>
<li>Explain foetal distress</li>
<li>Describe the different methods used in induction of labour</li>
<li>Describe management of prolonged labour</li>
<li>Explain the complications of prolonged labour</li>
<li>Describe the preventive measures of prolonged labour</li>
<li>Explain the concept of obstructed labour</li>
<li>Identify signs of obstructed labour</li>
<li>Describe the management of obstructed labour</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="trial-of-labour">Trial of Labour<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#trial-of-labour" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Trial of labour is a test of labour conducted where there is a minor or moderate degree of Cephalopelvic Disproportion (CPD) in which it is difficult to decide whether delivery per vagina is possible.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="factors-influencing-good-prognosis">Factors influencing good prognosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#factors-influencing-good-prognosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>There are several factors influencing good prognosis. These are:</p>
<ul>
<li>Strength of the uterine contractions</li>
<li>Flexion of the head</li>
<li>Degree of moulding of the foetal head, that is, reduced engaging diameters</li>
<li>The giving of pelvic joints. In pregnancy, the joints of the pelvis are relaxed and separate by half to one centimetre</li>
<li>Maternal courage</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="factors-influencing-poor-prognosis">Factors influencing poor prognosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#factors-influencing-poor-prognosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The factors influencing poor prognosis are:</p>
<ul>
<li>Early rupture of membrane which may be accompanied by prolapsed cord</li>
<li>Poor moulding of the head</li>
<li>Maternal or foetal distress which will necessitate intervention on trial of vaginal delivery</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Remember: Do not hesitate to terminate the trial of labour when there is foetal or maternal distress.</strong></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="contraindications-for-trial-of-labour">Contraindications for trial of labour<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#contraindications-for-trial-of-labour" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Compare the following list of contraindications for trial of labour with those you learnt in normal labour:</p>
<ul>
<li>Grossly contracted pelvis</li>
<li>Medical or obstetrical complications</li>
<li>Malpresentations, for example, breech</li>
<li>Elderly primigravida</li>
<li>Cases where trial of labour failed before</li>
<li>Cases of two previous caesarean sections</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Remember: Your encouragement and friendly attitude will boost the mother's morale.</strong></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management-of-trial-of-labour">Management of Trial of Labour<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-trial-of-labour" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Explain the situation to the mother and prepare her for possible operative intervention. Assess patient carefully on admission to ascertain the following:</p>
<ul>
<li>Whether the mother is in established labour</li>
<li>Presentation of foetus</li>
<li>Check for flexion of the head</li>
<li>State of foetal heart, that is, rate, rhythm and volume</li>
<li>General condition of mother physically and emotionally</li>
<li>Confine the mother to bed to prevent early rupture of membranes</li>
<li>Close observations of temperature and blood pressure every four hours</li>
<li>Observe foetal heart rate and maternal pulse quarterly to half hourly</li>
</ul>
<p>You should always observe for signs of foetal and maternal distress. Accurately observe and record for onset, strength, frequency and duration of the contractions. Closely observe the descent of the head every one to two hours per abdominal palpation by the same midwife if possible. Encourage the mother to pass urine</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>every two hours and test for acetone to exclude acidosis.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management-of-trial-of-labour">Management of Trial of Labour<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-trial-of-labour" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A vaginal examination should be done every four hours to assess the level of the presenting part, the degree moulding and flexion, the dilation of the cervix (whether progressive or not), the consistency of the cervix and the presence or absence of caput.</p>
<p>You should also check whether the membranes are intact or ruptured. Encourage adequate hydration by giving intravenous 5% dextrose. Sedate the mother with pethidine or morphia in early labour to promote rest, and reduce anxiety.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="undesirable-factors-in-trial-of-labour">Undesirable Factors in Trial of Labour<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#undesirable-factors-in-trial-of-labour" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Undesirable occurrences include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Rupture of membranes</li>
<li>Colour of liquor is meconium-stained</li>
<li>Uterine action is abnormal</li>
<li>Abnormal presentation, where there is a change from vertex to brow</li>
<li>When the presenting part fails to descend in spite of good uterine contraction</li>
<li>When there are signs of foetal or maternal distress</li>
</ul>
<p>Trial of labour may result in spontaneous vaginal delivery, assisted vaginal delivery by either forceps or vacuum, or caesarean section due to complications.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="trial-of-scar-vaginal-birth-after-caesarean-section">Trial of Scar: Vaginal Birth After Caesarean Section<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#trial-of-scar-vaginal-birth-after-caesarean-section" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Trial of scar is a test of labour for a woman with a previous caesarean section scar, where no recurrent indication is present.</p>
<p>Studies have shown that some 60 â€“ 65% of previous caesarean section mothers (Reedes/Martin, 1987) deliver per vagina, involving same or fewer risks than a repeated section. The trial should be in a facility where, if there is a need for a caesarean section, this can be performed immediately. The midwife should be vigilant in making the necessary observations.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-main-contraindications-to-trial-of-scar">The Main Contraindications to Trial of Scar<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-main-contraindications-to-trial-of-scar" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The main contraindications include:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Where the reason for the first scar is likely to be repeated, for example, in cephalopelvic disproportion</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Classical type of caesarean section</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Malpresentation, for example; breech</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Two previous caesarean section scars, regardless of the causes</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Where the previous scar wound did not heal with the first intention</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Where pregnancy occurs within six months of a caesarean section</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Where there is over-distension due to multiple pregnancy or hydromnious</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Multiparty</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>The management of this mother is as for trial of labour with the addition of these few points below:</p>
<ul>
<li>Palpate abdomen gently</li>
<li>Check for any tenderness over the scar</li>
<li>Observe for any signs of impending rupture of the uterus</li>
<li>Report any constant pain in abdomen</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="educating-the-patient-on-avoiding-unnecessary-caesarean-birth">Educating the Patient on Avoiding Unnecessary Caesarean Birth<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#educating-the-patient-on-avoiding-unnecessary-caesarean-birth" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A small percentage of women with conditions that are a threat to the foetal or maternal life need a caesarean section. Many other women have a caesarean section due to a series of events, which leads to an inevitable section seen as necessary at that particular time. For some, if other options had been discussed earlier, a caesarean section may have been avoided.</p>
<p>Some mothers insist on the operation if the month coincides with the previous month of birth of other children, so as to have the same birthdays for their babies. Others prefer not to push and go through the whole process of enlarging the birth canal. If these women were well informed, they might see the sense of preventing a caesarean section. Additional contributing factors to the decision to have a caesarean section include mismanagement of the syntocinon drip, choice of obstetrician and/or hospital policy.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="maternal-distress">Maternal Distress<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#maternal-distress" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is a serious and life threatening condition, which should not occur in this era. It happens when the metabolism and the electrolyte balance of the woman in labour is disturbed and this can result into ketoacidosis hypotonic uterine inertia. Maternal and foetal distresses usually occur together after prolonged labour.</p>
<p>In maternal distress, the accumulation of ketoacids and the electrolyte imbalance also</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 162 of 317
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>affect the metabolism and function of all the other muscles in the body. The intestines stop contracting, which is known as intestinal ileus. The large intestine (colon) distends. Emptying of the stomach is delayed. With large volumes of fluid stagnating uselessly in the stomach, and the small and large bowel, the woman becomes dehydrated. These disturbances in the mother result in a similar disturbance in the foetal metabolism. Often maternal and foetal distress present together in women who have been in labour for a long time at home and are brought to a health centre or hospital in poor condition.</p>
<p>The main symptoms of maternal distress are that the mother is exhausted by severe pain and lack of sleep and she might have severe abdominal pain because of the prolonged and obstructed labour.</p>
<ul>
<li>She displays signs of anxiety</li>
<li>She has a dry and furred tongue</li>
<li>Her pulse rate is over 120 beats per minute</li>
<li>Rapid and deep respiration because of acidosis</li>
<li>She has hot, dry and inelastic skin</li>
<li>She has a distended abdomen</li>
<li>There is a reduced output of highly concentrated urine</li>
<li>Her temperature is 38Â°C</li>
<li>She might already have a purulent discharge from an intrauterine infection due to early rupture of the membranes</li>
</ul>
<p>The main investigation is testing for the presence of acetone in the urine.</p>
<p>The management of Maternal Distress involves giving an infusion of 10% glucose to correct dehydration. A caesarean section is performed when in the first stage of labour. In the second stage, an episiotomy is given and delivery is assisted with vacuum extraction.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="foetal-distress">Foetal Distress<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#foetal-distress" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Foetal distress occurs when the foetus is deprived of oxygen and, as a result, develops hypoxia. The baby may be born as a still birth or develop asphyxia and suffer brain damage.</p>
