<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="causes-of-foetal-distress">Causes of Foetal Distress<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causes-of-foetal-distress" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Congenital malformation</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Problems with the cord, for example, prolapse, true knot, twisted round the neck</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Obstetric complications</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Mother's condition of preeclampsia/eclampsia</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Severe anaemia, APH</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Intra-partum causes include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Prolonged labour</li>
<li>Malpresentation and malposition</li>
<li>Shoulder dystocia</li>
</ul>
<p>Foetal tachycardia of more than 160 per minute is an early sign while foetal bradycardia or pulse less than 120 beats per minute is a late sign of foetal distress. Foetal heart acceleration related with uterine contraction is another sign of foetal distress.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management-of-foetal-distress">Management of Foetal Distress<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-foetal-distress" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>When foetal distress is anticipated, a blood sample is taken, the normal pH being 7.35. If this falls to 7.2, labour has to be terminated. Below pH 7 the brain cells perish. When there are signs of foetal distress, call the doctor. If the mother is on an oxytocin drip, stop it immediately. Change the mother's position and give oxygen by facemask. If the mother is in the first stage of labour, a caesarean section should be performed.</p>
<p>If she is in the second stage, an episiotomy should be given. Forceps or vacuum hastens the birth. A paediatrician should always be present, if possible.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="post-term-pregnancy">Post Term Pregnancy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#post-term-pregnancy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Prolonged pregnancy, or post term pregnancy, refers to a pregnancy that has exceeded 294 days from the first day of the last menstrual period. The difference between this term and post maturity or post mature is that the latter relates to the baby and refers to features or conditions of the neonate.</p>
<p>It has been proven that the duration of pregnancy differs depending on parity and race. Primagravidae have a longer duration of 288 days, compared to multigravidae, who normally have a duration of about 283 days.</p>
<p>To determine prolonged pregnancy is not easy as the mother may give wrong dates. Assessing the gestation period by clinical estimation can be inaccurate because of the biological variation in the size of the mother and the foetus. Quickening cannot be relied on as there is a range of weeks. A primagravida may start feeling quickening between 15-22 weeks while a multigravida may feel quickening at 14-22 weeks. An ultrasound may be relied on in the</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 163 of 317
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>assessment of maturity. Early scanning can also help to reduce the mistake of diagnosing prolonged pregnancy.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="risks-of-post-term-pregnancy">Risks of Post Term Pregnancy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#risks-of-post-term-pregnancy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>There is low prenatal mortality at 40 weeks, which increases at 42 weeks. The post term period contributes to foetal maturation, with big babies weighing 4,000gm in 10% of cases and 4,500gm in 1% of cases. This can result in cephalopelvic disproportion or shoulder dystocia. There is a reduction of amniotic fluid, which may result in cord compression and reduction of the placental function. There is also a high risk of foetal distress. The management of post term pregnancy usually involves induction of labour (Myles 1999).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="induction-of-labour">Induction of Labour<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#induction-of-labour" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Induction of labour involves the initiation of uterine muscle contraction by artificial means.</p>
<p><strong>Remember: Make sure that when labour is induced it will result in a viable baby.</strong></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="indications">Indications<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#indications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>When the health or well being of the mother or the foetus would be endangered if the pregnancy continues</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Prolonged pregnancy because after 42 weeks there is danger of placental insufficiency</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Preeclampsia, where both mother and baby are in danger, with the mother in danger of eclampsia and the baby in danger of placental insufficiency</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Signs of intrauterine growth, retardation, which can be detected by abdominal examination or serial ultrasound scan</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Placental insufficiency more common in primigravida aged over 35 years</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Poor obstetric history, for example, history of stillbirth or intra uterine growth retardation in previous pregnancies</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Polyhydramnious, foetal abnormalities</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Spontaneous rupture of membranes. If membranes rupture spontaneously after 36 weeks gestation and labour does not commence within 12 hours, danger of intra uterine infection is very high</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Previous large baby, where weight was over 4kg. Induction is indicated between 38 - 40 weeks. Foetal size tends to increase with successive pregnancies</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Diabetes mellitus, noting that intrauterine death tends to occur near term so induction is indicated between 36 - 38 weeks</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Rhesus iso-immunisation, where rhesus antibodies are present in the maternal serum and the titre is high, labour should be induced to save the life of the baby</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Unstable lie when placenta praevia and pelvic abnormalities have been excluded</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Genital herpes, where labour is usually induced after 38 weeks gestation if disease is in remission</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Previous precipitate labour which tends to recur so induction is indicated at 38 weeks</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Social reasons, which is not common in our community but occurs sometimes</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Intrauterine death</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="foetal-maturity-and-viability">Foetal Maturity and Viability<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#foetal-maturity-and-viability" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Where possible amniocentesis may be performed. The lecithin to sphingomyelin ratio in the liquor is calculated in order to estimate the foetal pulmonary maturity. When the ratio is less than two to one, it means that the lungs are not yet mature and induction of labour should be delayed. At times, steroids are given to the mother to stimulate the foetal lungs to produce surfactant to reduce the risk of RDS (Respiratory Distress Syndrome).</p>
<p><strong>Remember:</strong></p>
<p>You must also make sure you have excluded any contraindications for induction of labour.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="contraindications-for-the-induction-of-labour">Contraindications for the Induction of Labour<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#contraindications-for-the-induction-of-labour" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Cephalopelvic disproportion</li>
<li>Unreliable estimated date of delivery. Confirm estimated date of delivery and maturity by ultrasound</li>
<li>Malpresentation</li>
<li>Oblique or transverse lie</li>
<li>Foetal compromise, that is, if the foetus could not stand the uterine contractions due to prematurity or placenta insufficiency. In such cases caesarean section is preferred</li>
<li>Psychological factors, for example, if the mother is against induction, her decision should be respected</li>
</ul>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<ul>
<li>Placenta previa</li>
</ul>
<p>Favourable factors for induction include:</p>
<ul>
<li>38 or more weeks of gestation</li>
<li>Bishop's score of six or more</li>
<li>Where 3/5ths of the head or less is palpable above the pelvic brim</li>
</ul>
<p>here are different methods of induction, which are:</p>
<ul>
<li>Medical, where drugs alone are used and the amniotic sac remains intact</li>
<li>Surgical, where the membranes are artificially ruptured</li>
<li>A combination of medical and surgical intervention</li>
</ul>
<p>You will now explore each of these methods in more detail.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="medical-induction">Medical Induction<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#medical-induction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Intravaginal prostaglandin E2 are used in the form of pessaries (2.5mg), vaginal tablets (3-6mg) or gel (2.5-5mg). A nelatone urinary catheter is attached to a syringe containing the gel while membranes are intact in case of intrauterine infection. Introduce the gel to the posterior vaginal phornix.</p>
<p>The dose varies from 2.5mg-5mg. If there is no change overnight, prostaglandin may be added/repeated, but if the cervix ripens overnight, then pessaries of prostaglandin E2 may be introduced to the vagina.</p>
<p>The following steps should be taken to ensure adequate care of the mother during the procedure:</p>
<ul>
<li>Maximum of an hour is needed to allow absorption of the prostaglandin, so the mother should be asked to stay in for this period</li>
<li>Observations are carried out as in normal labour</li>
<li>After one hour, if foetal heart is normal, the mother should be allowed to walk around</li>
<li>After four hours, if labour has not been established, a vaginal examination should be done to reassess the cervical dilatation</li>
<li>If there has been some progress, artificial rupture of the membranes is done and a syntocinon drip is commenced two hours later to prevent sensitivity of the uterus</li>
</ul>
<p>Oral prostaglandin is usually used to induce labour where the membranes have ruptured. One tablet is swallowed at an hourly interval. A</p>
<p>maximum of ten tablets should be administered. Each tablet contains 0.5mg of prostaglandin E2. Should it cause diarrhoea, the administration should be stopped immediately.</p>
<p>You should note, however, that there are several complications associated with prostaglandin. The mother may suffer discomfort due to painful contractions. The induction may be ineffective. Over-stimulation of the uterus can cause foetal and maternal distress.</p>
<p>Another variety of medical induction is oxytocin administration. The amount and rate of oxytocin must be carefully calculated and administered. Usually 5% dextrose in water of 500mls with five units of syntocinon is commenced after a vaginal examination. The drip is started at 15 drops per minute and increased by ten drops after every half-hour to a maximum of 60 drops. Using two bottles of the same solution is preferred so that in the event of discontinuation of oxytocin, the intravenous line will still be open.</p>
<p>It is crucial to label the amount of syntocinon put in both the bottle and the 2.5ml IV for multiparous and 5ml IV for primigravida chart.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="factors-which-should-be-observed-and-recorded-during-oxytocin-infusion">Factors Which Should be Observed and Recorded During Oxytocin Infusion<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#factors-which-should-be-observed-and-recorded-during-oxytocin-infusion" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Dosage of oxytocin, the name and amount of solution</li>
<li>Rate of flow</li>
<li>Vital signs and foetal heart rate every 15-30 minutes</li>
<li>Vaginal examination findings four hourly</li>
<li>Maintain intake and output chart</li>
<li>Record in the chart any other treatment that is given</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="possible-complications-of-oxytocin-use">Possible Complications of Oxytocin Use<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#possible-complications-of-oxytocin-use" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Hypertonic uterine contraction causing foetal distress</li>
<li>Tetanic and tumultuous contractions, which can result in abruptio placenta</li>
<li>Birth injury due to rapid expulsion of the baby</li>
<li>Mother may develop hypertension with frontal headache</li>
</ul>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>Remember:
If any one of the above signs occurs, stop the syntocinon drip immediately and inform the doctor.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="medical-induction">Medical Induction<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#medical-induction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The Bishop Score is an objective method of assessing whether the cervix is favourable for induction of labour. The table below shows how the score is calculated.</p>
<p>Bishop Score Table</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Scores</th><th></th><th></th><th></th><th></th><th></th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Inducibility features</td><td></td><td>0</td><td>1</td><td>2</td><td>3</td></tr><tr><td>1</td><td>Consistency of cervix</td><td>Firm</td><td>Medium</td><td>Soft</td><td>-</td></tr><tr><td>2</td><td>Position of cervix</td><td>Posterior</td><td>Mid</td><td>Anterior</td><td>-</td></tr><tr><td>3</td><td>Length of cervix in cm</td><td>&gt;2</td><td>2</td><td>1</td><td>&lt;0.5</td></tr><tr><td></td><td>(or Effacement)</td><td>(0-30%)</td><td>(40-50%)</td><td>(60-70%)</td><td>(80%+)</td></tr><tr><td>4</td><td>Dilatation of cervix</td><td>Closed</td><td>1-2cm</td><td>3-4cm</td><td>5cm+</td></tr><tr><td>5</td><td>Station of presenting part 1 cm above or below ischial spines</td><td>-3</td><td>-2</td><td>-1,0</td><td>3</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Each score is awarded 0 - 3 and the range of scores is 0 - 13. A total score of six or over is favourable. However a score of nine or more will have a safe, successful induction with an estimated length of labour of less than four hours.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="surgical-induction-amniotomy">Surgical Induction (Amniotomy)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#surgical-induction-amniotomy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In the case of an uncomplicated pregnancy, a sweep of the membranes is an effective method of inducing labour. After a vaginal examination, the index finger is swept through the cervical os to detach foetal membranes from the deciduas. The action produces prostaglandin.</p>
<p>Amniotomy is an Artificial Rupture of the Membranes (ARM), which is carried out to induce labour when the cervix is favourable. A well fitting presenting part is essential to avoid prolapse of the cord or rupture of the membranes. Allow the descent of the presenting part to the cervical os. This raises the level of prostaglandin which stimulates strong contractions to hasten labour. This method of induction may be combined with oxytocin drip and this is referred to as combined method. This method has likelihood of delivery within 12 hours, requires less analgesia and reduces the risk of Post Partum Haemorrhage (PPH).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="hazards-associated-with-artificial-rupture-of-membranes-arm">Hazards Associated with Artificial Rupture of Membranes (ARM)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hazards-associated-with-artificial-rupture-of-membranes-arm" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Intrauterine infection due to contaminated instruments</li>
<li>Cord prolapse</li>
<li>Early foetal heart deceleration</li>
<li>Bleeding due to vasa or placenta previa</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="remember">Remember:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#remember" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Due to the potential risks of this method, it is now being discouraged in this era of HIV/AIDS.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="prolonged-labour">Prolonged Labour<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prolonged-labour" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The term 'prolonged labour' is used when delivery does not take place after 12 hours of established labour (Baird 1952, Myles 1999). Different terms are used for prolonged labour at different times or for different reasons.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="prolonged-latent-stage">Prolonged Latent Stage<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prolonged-latent-stage" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The latent phase lasts from the onset of labour to three centimetre dilatation of the cervical os. If this phase takes more than 20 hours in a primigravida and more than 14 hours in a multigravida, it is considered prolonged. In practice diagnosis should be suspected and treatment instituted many hours before this time interval has elapsed.</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 167 of 317
Bishop's Computers</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="primary-dysfunctional-labour">Primary Dysfunctional Labour<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#primary-dysfunctional-labour" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>This is when active phase of labour is slow and the cervix dilates at less than one centimetre per hour.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="secondary-arrest">Secondary Arrest<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#secondary-arrest" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>This is when there is slow cervical dilatation in the active phase after normal progress in early labour.</p>
<p>There are numerous causes of prolonged labour at each stage.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="causes-of-prolonged-first-stage-of-labour">Causes of Prolonged First Stage of Labour<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causes-of-prolonged-first-stage-of-labour" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Poor uterine contractions, leading to the cervix dilating slowly or not at all</li>
<li>Pelvic abnormalities (passage), where contracted pelvis and tumours of the pelvis cause poor progress in labour</li>
<li>The foetus (passenger) is a large baby, or there is malposition or malpresentation, which prevent the descent of the foetus, for example, occipito-posterior position or shoulder presentation</li>
<li>Psychological causes, for instance; tension and fear of the unknown tend to prolong labour, most commonly in women who are primigravidae</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="causes-of-prolonged-second-stage-of-labour">Causes of Prolonged Second Stage of Labour<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causes-of-prolonged-second-stage-of-labour" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Secondary hypotonic contractions may cause a delay</li>
<li>Poor maternal effort, which could be due to fear, exhaustion or lack of sensation due to epidural block, which may inhibit the woman's ability to bear down</li>
<li>A rigid perineum, which may prevent the advance of the foetus. During the perineal phase, an episiotomy should be performed at the height a contraction</li>
<li>Reduced pelvic outlet, as in the android pelvis, which narrows at the outlet due to its prominent ischial spines and narrowed sub-pubic arch</li>
<li>A large foetus, malposition or malpresentation, leading to a large presenting diameter, accounting for the delay</li>
</ul>
<p>Remember: You should reassure the mother at all times during labour.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="diagnosis-of-prolonged-labour">Diagnosis of Prolonged Labour<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnosis-of-prolonged-labour" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Now that you have seen the possible causes of prolonged labour, you will now focus on the diagnosis of prolonged labour. The following methods may be used to diagnose prolonged labour:</p>
<ul>
<li>Proper history of labour including type, duration and frequency of uterine contractions</li>
<li>Examination of the mother, checking for general appearance, whether distressed or exhausted</li>
<li>Check the temperature and pulse as an increase of either of them would be significant</li>
<li>Urinalysis, where concentrated urine suggests fluid imbalance and dehydration. Check for ketones in the urine, the presence of this must be corrected at once</li>
<li>It is important to identify the cause in order to decide the course of action.</li>
</ul>
<p>Management of prolonged labour involves management as in normal labour but with some additional steps.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="additional-steps-required-in-the-management-of-prolonged-labour">Additional Steps Required in the Management of Prolonged Labour<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#additional-steps-required-in-the-management-of-prolonged-labour" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>When progress of labour is delayed due to poor uterine contractions, syntocinon drip must be put up. If there is no progress in spite of good uterine contraction, labour should be terminated by caesarean section</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Assist the mother to adopt a comfortable position</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Start an intravenous infusion to correct dehydration and ketosis, for example, Ringer's lactate solution or 5% dextrose</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Encourage the mother to empty her bladder every two hours and test the urine for ketones to exclude maternal distress</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Maintain a fluid input and output chart</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Allow sips of water if absolutely necessary even in anticipation of general anaesthesia</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Give oral ranitidine (zantac) 15mg every six hours to reduce gastric secretions</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Give broad-spectrum antibiotic if membranes rupture early (within 24 hours)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Observe and record every two to four hours temperature, pulse, respiration and blood pressure</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Contractions should be recorded every 15 to 30 minutes and take care of the bladder every two hours</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="foetal-condition-in-prolonged-labour">Foetal Condition in Prolonged Labour<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#foetal-condition-in-prolonged-labour" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The following steps should be taken to monitor the foetal condition:</p>
<ul>
<li>Monitor the foetal heart continuously every quarter to half hour.</li>
<li>Observe the amniotic fluid for presence of meconium to rule out foetal distress.</li>
<li>For secondary hypotonic uterine contraction, commence an intravenous infusion of syntocinon with 10% dextrose to stimulate adequate contractions</li>
<li>Ensure that the presenting part is visible before encouraging the mother to push.</li>
<li>Perform an episiotomy under local anaesthesia or at the height of a contraction if the perineum is rigid.</li>
<li>If the cause was obstruction at the outlet as in android pelvis, and the head is arrested mid pelvis resulting to foetal distress, caesarean section is recommended.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="complications-of-prolonged-labour">Complications of Prolonged Labour<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#complications-of-prolonged-labour" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>There are a number of complications, which may be experienced by both the mother and the foetus during a prolonged labour.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="maternal-complications">Maternal complications<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#maternal-complications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Oedema of the pelvic floor due to the pressure of the presenting part on the pelvic floor and the vaginal walls</li>
<li>Retention of urine due to continuous compression of the urethra by the presenting part causing bruising which might persist during puerperium</li>
<li>Ruptured uterus due to overstretching of the lower uterine segment</li>
<li>Deep perineal tears due to overstretching of the perineum, leading to cystocele or rectocele</li>
<li>The overstretching of the pelvic floor and uterine ligaments may also cause uterine prolapse</li>
<li>Stress incontinence</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="foetal-complications">Foetal complications<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#foetal-complications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Intra cranial damage due to excessive moulding</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Foetal hypoxia, which will lead to asphyxia</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Intra cranial haemorrhage due to prolonged compression of the head, and difficult instrumental delivery</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="prevention-of-prolonged-labour">Prevention of Prolonged Labour<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prevention-of-prolonged-labour" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Good prenatal care is essential to prevent prolonged labour. This includes:</p>
<ul>
<li>Taking a proper history in relation to cases of previous difficult deliveries</li>
<li>Detection of malpresentation and malposition</li>
<li>Any sign of contracted pelvis should be referred to the obstetrician in time to make a timely decision on the mode of delivery</li>
</ul>
<p>During labour you should take the following steps:</p>
<ul>
<li>Maintain proper partograph of the mother in labour and take early decision</li>
<li>Ensure proper control of the syntocinon drip</li>
<li>Ensure bladder is emptied every two hours to avoid delay of labour</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="obstructed-labour">Obstructed Labour<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#obstructed-labour" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Labour is obstructed when there is no advance of the presenting part in spite of strong uterine contractions further progress is impossible without assistance. Usually the power (contractions) involves the passage (the birth canal) and the passenger (the foetus). Obstruction usually occurs at the pelvic brim, but may occur at the outlet, for example, in an android pelvis.</p>
<p>Compare the causes of obstructed labour with those of prolonged labour. In obstructed labour, the problem is the passenger and passage (never the power). Usually this is when the passenger has gross abnormalities. This is the opposite of prolonged labour where the 'power' may be the main issue and the passenger or passage have mild or moderate problem.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-main-causes-of-obstructed-labour">The Main Causes of Obstructed Labour<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-main-causes-of-obstructed-labour" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Cephalopelvic disproportion</li>
</ul>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<ul>
<li>Malpresentation, for example; shoulder, brow presentation or persistent mentoposterior position</li>
<li>Fibroids or tumours located in the lower uterine segment</li>
<li>Cervical dystocia</li>
<li>Gross foetal abnormalities e.g. hydrocephalus, locked twins</li>
<li>Disordered uterine action</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="diagnosis-of-obstruction-of-labour">Diagnosis of Obstruction of Labour<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnosis-of-obstruction-of-labour" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="early-signs">Early Signs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#early-signs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>The presenting part does not enter the pelvic brim despite good uterine contraction</li>
<li>The cervix dilates slowly and hangs loosely like an empty sleeve due to poor application of the presenting part</li>
<li>The membranes tend to rupture early</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="later-signs">Later Signs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#later-signs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Foetal and maternal distress, which occur concurrently</li>
<li>The contractions are hypertonic and the mother does not relax in between them</li>
<li>The uterus is moulded around the foetus</li>
<li>The mother may have pyrexia and tachycardia</li>
<li>On vaginal examination, there is presence of large caput</li>
<li>The vagina feels hot and dry and the cervix and vulva are oedematous</li>
<li>In cephalic presentation, the presenting part becomes wedged and immovable when it descends partly into the pelvis</li>
<li>It is difficult to pass urine, if catheterised, the urine is bloodstained due to the bruised urethra</li>
<li>Urinary output is poor</li>
<li>Uterine exhaustion occurs and contractions cease for a while, only to recommence with renewed vigour, especially in primigravida</li>
<li>A Bandle's ring is seen abdominally as the lower segment is progressively enlarged and thinned out and the upper segment becomes shorter and thick</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="prevention-of-obstruction-of-labour">Prevention of Obstruction of Labour<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prevention-of-obstruction-of-labour" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Obstructed labour can be prevented through the following measures:</p>
<ul>
<li>Good prenatal care to detect mothers at risk</li>
<li>Clinical and radiological investigations of pelvis adequacy if necessary during the prenatal period</li>
<li>Careful assessment of the progress throughout labour to detect lack of descent before labour is obstructed</li>
<li>Taking and interpreting vital observations during labour. This includes foetal heart rate, maternal pulse, temperature and blood pressure, assessment of length, strength and duration of uterine contractions, cervical dilatation four hourly</li>
<li>Alert an obstetrician immediately, If obstructed labour is suspected</li>
<li>Commence an intravenous infusion if not already commenced</li>
<li>Take blood for grouping and cross match in case transfusion is needed. (Keep ready two units of blood) catheterise to empty the urinary bladder</li>
<li>Maintain asepsis techniques to prevent infection</li>
<li>In case of early rupture of membranes, give prophylactic antibiotic (as ordered by the doctor)</li>
<li>Give pre-medication as per doctor's order (Pethidine 100mg IM stat)</li>
<li>Prepare the mother for emergency caesarean section if in the first stage of labour</li>
</ul>
<p>In the second stage of labour, failure to progress may be caused by deep transverse arrest. If obstruction cannot be overcome by rotation and assisted birth, a caesarean section should be performed as soon as possible.</p>
<p>The newborn unit should be informed to prepare to receive an asphyxiated baby. Resuscitation equipment should be kept ready and a paediatrician should be present at birth. The surgeon will check carefully for any indication that the uterus has ruptured before taking the patient to theatre for repair of the uterus.</p>
<p>If the labour is obstructed and the foetus has died, the mode of delivery will still be caesarean section, as vaginal birth cannot be achieved.</p>
<p>The following advice should be given to mothers on the prevention of obstructed labour:</p>
<ul>
<li>Mothers should attend antenatal clinic as soon as they realise they are pregnant</li>
</ul>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 169 of 317
Bishop's Computers</p>
<ul>
<li>All mothers who have had a previous caesarean section should have a hospital delivery</li>
<li>Discourage home deliveries, especially of primigravidae and grand multiparous</li>
<li>Educate traditional birth attendants on early signs of obstructed labour</li>
<li>Provide health education to the community on the risks of too early or too late pregnancies</li>
<li>Advise pregnant mothers on the importance of a well balanced diet</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="complications-occurring-in-obstruction-of-labour">Complications Occurring in Obstruction of Labour<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#complications-occurring-in-obstruction-of-labour" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>There are a number of complications, which may be experienced by both the mother and the foetus during obstructed labour.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="maternal-complications">Maternal complications<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#maternal-complications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Rupture of the uterus, due to excessive thinning of the lower uterine segment</li>
<li>The bladder is traumatised by pressure of the foetal head during labour and delivery. When the bladder or rectum is bruised, this may cause vesico-vaginal fistula or recto-vaginal fistula</li>
<li>Injury due to a difficult instrumental delivery</li>
<li>Urinary incontinence due to prolonged compression of tissues causing necrosis of the bladder</li>
<li>Prolonged rupture of membranes may cause intra uterine infection</li>
<li>Maternal death occurs when operative delivery is carried out before shock and dehydration is corrected</li>
<li>Death can also occur in ruptured uterus due to haemorrhage. You will discuss this in greater detail in the section on Obstetric Emergencies.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="foetal-complications">Foetal complications<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#foetal-complications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Intrauterine asphyxia, leading to intracranial damage, that is, permanent brain damage or stillbirth</li>
<li>Intracranial haemorrhage</li>
<li>Neonatal pneumonia due to ascending infection resulting from meconium aspiration</li>
<li>Neonatal death</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="malposition-of-occiput-and-malpresentation">Malposition of Occiput and Malpresentation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#malposition-of-occiput-and-malpresentation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The foetus is not always in the desired position or lie in the uterus. As a result of malposition there is malpresentation of the foetus. The midwife needs to be aware of the various possible malpresentations their complications and how to manage the situation. Several malpositions of the occiput and malpresentations in general are discussed in the following pages.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="occipito-posterior-position">Occipito Posterior Position<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#occipito-posterior-position" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Occipito posterior position is a malposition of the occiput. In this position, the vertex is present but it occupies the posterior position instead of the anterior. The occipito posterior position can be either left or right. The cause is not clear but it is associated with abnormalities of the pelvis.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260112-6b42bc1c.jpeg" alt="img-5.jpeg">
Right (A) and left (B) occipito posterior position.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260112-6c3f1820.jpeg" alt="img-6.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="diagnosis-of-occipito-posterior-position">Diagnosis of Occipito Posterior Position<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnosis-of-occipito-posterior-position" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>On inspection of the abdomen you will notice a saucer shaped depression at or below the umbilicus. The unengaged head will outline the bladder as if it is a full bladder.</p>
<p>On palpation the head is high, as the engaged diameter of 11.5cm cannot enter the brim until flexion takes place. The head feels large and the occiput and sinciput are on the same level. The back is difficult to palpate. Limbs are felt on both sides of the abdomen.</p>
<p>On auscultation the foetal heart is heard on the right flank. It could also be heard at the umbilicus, either at the middle line or slightly to the left.</p>
<p>During labour the mother may complain of severe backache. You may note a slow descent of the presenting part in spite of good</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>contractions. Early rupture of membrane may occur.</p>
<p>On vaginal examination the diagnosis can be confirmed on feeling the anterior fontanelle to the left anterior in ROP. The Sagittal sutures will be in the right oblique of the pelvis, but the findings will depend on the degree of flexion of the head.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management-of-labour-in-the-occipito-posterior-position">Management of Labour in the Occipito Posterior Position<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-labour-in-the-occipito-posterior-position" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In the occipito posterior position you should expect prolonged, painful labour due to poor fitting of the presenting part, which does not stimulate good contractions.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="first-stage-of-labour">First Stage of Labour<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#first-stage-of-labour" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The mother may experience severe backache. You should give a back massage and encourage the mother to remain mobile as long as she can and to adopt what ever position that is most comfortable to her. Most women find the all-fours position most comfortable, pain relieving and is also believed to aid in the rotation of the foetal head. Labour is prolonged with incoordinate uterine action. Give intravenous fluid to ensure that the mother is not dehydrated.</p>
<p>Uterine action should be regulated by the use of syntocinon. Keep accurate records by plotting half-hourly observations of the foetal heart, contractions every four hours, and blood pressure in the partograph. Maintain a strict intake and output chart. The mother may have the urge of early pushing due to the occiput pressing on the rectum. You should discourage her from pushing at this stage as this will cause the cervix to be oedematous and delay the onset of the second stage. Encourage her to change her position and use breathing techniques, as these will control the urge of early pushing.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="second-stage-of-labour">Second Stage of Labour<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#second-stage-of-labour" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The second stage should be confirmed by vaginal examination as the caput may be seen at the vulva with the anterior lip of the cervix. During labour, one of the following may occur:</p>
<ul>
<li>Long internal rotation</li>
<li>Short internal rotation</li>
<li>Deep transverse arrest</li>
</ul>
<p>The second stage of labour can present any of three conditions which you will now explore in detail.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="long-internal-rotation">Long Internal Rotation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#long-internal-rotation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is where the head turns 3/8 of a circle in 90% of cases and the baby is born as in occiput anterior.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="characteristics-of-long-internal-rotation">Characteristics of Long Internal Rotation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#characteristics-of-long-internal-rotation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>The lie is longitudinal</li>
<li>The attitude is one of deflexion</li>
<li>The presentation is vertex</li>
<li>The presenting part is the middle or anterior area of the left pariental bone</li>
<li>The position is right occipito posterior</li>
<li>The denominator is the occiput</li>
<li>The occipito frontal diameter 11.5cm lies in the right oblique diameter of the pelvic brim</li>
<li>The occiput points at the right sacroiliac joints and the sinciput points at the left iliopectineal eminence</li>
<li>There is increased flexion and descent takes place in the occiput head and reaches the pelvic floor</li>
<li>Internal rotation of the head occurs which rotates 3/8 of a circle on the right side of the pelvis while the shoulder rotates 2/8 of a circle on the same side</li>
<li>The head crowns</li>
<li>The sinciput, face and chin sweep the perineum, the head is born by extension</li>
<li>Restitution where the occiput turns 1/8 to the right, undoes the twist at the neck and rights itself with the shoulder</li>
<li>Internal rotation of the shoulders. The shoulder enters in the same oblique diameter of the pelvis. Anterior shoulder reaches the pelvic floor and rotates 1/8 of a circle forward and lies under the symphysis pubis</li>
<li>External rotation of the head accompanies the internal rotation of the shoulder</li>
<li>Anterior shoulder escapes under the symphysis pubis, while the posterior shoulder sweeps the perineum</li>
<li>The body is born by movement of lateral flexion</li>
</ul>
<p>Remember: The above movements do not differ much from the normal mechanism as you may have noticed.</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 172 of 317
Bishop's Computers</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="short-rotation">Short Rotation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#short-rotation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>In cases of short rotation or persistent occiput posterior position, the occiput fails to rotate forward. It persists with the same position. The sincipit reaches the pelvic floor and rotates forwards, while the occiput sinks in the hollow of the sacrum.</p>
<p>The baby is born face to pubis.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management-of-face-to-pubis-delivery">Management of Face to Pubis Delivery<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-face-to-pubis-delivery" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Give an episiotomy when necessary:</p>
<p>You should watch for signs of buttonhole tear due to the large presenting diameter. A buttonhole tear is a rupture at the centre of the perineum.</p>
<p>If you failed to diagnose this earlier you may be extending the head thinking it is a vertex delivery, until you see the hairless forehead escaping under the pubis arch. You should then flex the head towards the symphysis pubis.</p>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Sincipit will emerge. You should hold the sincipit back to maintain flexion which will allow the occiput to sweep the perineum.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Now let the occiput sweep the perineum and be born first.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260112-c41f182b.jpeg" alt="img-7.jpeg"></p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260112-33d63f26.jpeg" alt="img-8.jpeg"></p>
<ol start="3">
<li>
<p>Get hold of vertex and bring the face downwards under the symphysis pubis.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Now extend the head and let the sincipit, face and chin sweep the perenium and the face is born by extension.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260112-ec26685c.jpeg" alt="img-9.jpeg"></p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260112-d97e9844.jpeg" alt="img-10.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="deep-transverse-arrest">Deep Transverse Arrest<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#deep-transverse-arrest" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>This is where the occiput fails to rotate forward. This forces the sincipit to reach the pelvic floor first and rotate forwards. The occiput then goes into the hollow of the sacrum, which results in the face to pubis delivery. At first there is good flexion. The occipit reaches the pelvic floor and begins to rotate but flexion is not maintained. The occipito frontal diameter is caught by the bispinious diameter of the outlet. This arrest may be due to poor contractions, a straight sacrum or prominent ischial spines.</p>
<p>On vaginal examination the sagittal suture is on the transverse diameter of the pelvis and both anterior and posterior fontanels are palpable. The head is caught at the ischial spines.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management-of-deep-transverse-arrest">Management of Deep Transverse Arrest<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-deep-transverse-arrest" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Reassure the mother while explaining the position of her labour. Take her consent for the operative procedures which will be necessary. Inform the doctor of her situation. Encourage her to breathe slowly and change her position to discourage pushing. When the doctor arrives, administer analgesics. A vacuum extraction may be performed or the head may be rotated with forceps and the baby delivered.</p>
<p>Aftercare is the same as in operative manipulation.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="conversion-to-face-or-brow">Conversion to Face or Brow<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#conversion-to-face-or-brow" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>At the onset of labour with a deflexed head, an extension may occur instead of flexion. When there is complete extension, the baby will be born as face presentation but when there is incomplete extension (this is referred to as 'military attitude'), the presenting part turns to brow. A delivery by caesarean section is recommended.</p>
<p>You have seen that labour is not smooth with this type of malposition.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="complications-of-conversion-to-face-or-brow">Complications of Conversion to Face or Brow<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#complications-of-conversion-to-face-or-brow" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Obstructed labour, as a result of deflexed or partially extended head that is impacted in the pelvis</li>
<li>Maternal trauma, as a result of prolonged labour, or instrumental delivery causing perineum tears. In undiagnosed OPP, instrumental delivery may cause third degree tears</li>
<li>Neonatal trauma to the baby, if forceps or ventous vacuum extraction are used</li>
<li>Cord prolapse which may cause hypoxia, that may result in stillbirth</li>
<li>Cerebral haemorrhage, due to the compression of a large presenting part</li>
<li>Asphyxia, leading to brain damage</li>
</ul>
<p>You will now look at face presentation as it is one of the potential OPP outcomes. Note the delivery of face in comparison with face to pubis.</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 173 of 317
Bishop's Computers</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="face-presentation">Face Presentation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#face-presentation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Face presentation occurs when the head has complete extension, and the occiput is in contact with its spine. It happens in about one in every five hundred labours. Primary face presentation is when the face presents before labour. The term secondary face presentation is used when the face presents during labour. There are six positions in a face presentation, namely:</p>
<ul>
<li>Right mento-posterior</li>
<li>Left mento-posterior</li>
<li>Right mento-lateral</li>
<li>Left mento-lateral</li>
<li>Right mento-anterior</li>
<li>Left mento-anterior</li>
</ul>
<p>The denominator is the mento, the presenting diameters are the submento bregmatic (9.5cm) and the bi-temporal (8.2cm).</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260112-bc03c174.jpeg" alt="img-11.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="causes-of-face-presentation">Causes of Face Presentation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causes-of-face-presentation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>You will now look at some of the causes of face presentation in detail.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="anterior-obliquity-of-the-uterus">Anterior Obliquity of the Uterus<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#anterior-obliquity-of-the-uterus" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The pendulous abdomen of a multiparous woman leans forward resulting in the alteration of the direction of the uterine axis. This causes the foetal buttocks to also lean forward and the force of the contractions to be directed in a line towards the chin, rather than occiput, which usually results in extension of the head.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="contracted-pelvis">Contracted Pelvis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#contracted-pelvis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Face presentation develops as the head enters in the transverse diameter of the brim. The obstetric conjugate is bound to be withheld which will result in the extended head in an android pelvis. Face presentation results when vertex presentation is in the posterior position and remains deflexed. The parietal eminences are caught in the reduced sacro-cotyloid dimension, the occiput does not descend and the head becomes extended.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="polyhydramnios">Polyhydramnios<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#polyhydramnios" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>In polyhydramnios, when the spontaneous rupture of membranes occurs, the resulting rush of fluids may cause the head to extend as it sinks into the lower uterine segment.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="congenital-abnormality">Congenital Abnormality<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#congenital-abnormality" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The absence of vertex in the encephally thrusts the face forwards. A tumour on the foetal neck can also cause extension of the head although this is rare.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="abdominal-and-per-vaginal-diagnosis-of-a-face-presentation">Abdominal and Per Vaginal Diagnosis of a Face Presentation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#abdominal-and-per-vaginal-diagnosis-of-a-face-presentation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The diagnosis is usually made in labour. During an abdominal examination check for the following features:</p>
<ul>
<li>The shape of the foetal spine is an s-shape.</li>
<li>The round occiput is prominent and may be ballottable when the position is mento-posterior and a deep groove can be felt between it and the back.</li>
</ul>
<p>The diagnosis is not always easy and clear. During a vaginal examination you may notice that you can diagnose face presentation with confidence if you have mastered vaginal examination skills. You will differentiate face from brow presentation when you feel the orbital ridges, the brow itself and the anterior sutures. You should look for the following characteristics:</p>
<ul>
<li>The presenting part is usually high, soft and irregular</li>
<li>In a sufficiently dilated cervix you may feel orbital ridges, eyes, nose and mouth</li>
<li>The mouth may be open with hard gums</li>
<li>The foetus may suck the examining finger</li>
<li>In progressive labour, the face becomes oedematous and is difficult to distinguish it from a breech presentation</li>
<li>To determine the mentum, you must locate it, and if it is posterior, you should decide whether it is lower than the sinciput in order to rotate forward and advance</li>
<li>The orbit ridges determine the position either on the left or right oblique of the pelvis brim</li>
</ul>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 174 of 317
Bishop's Computers</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="mechanism-of-left-mento-anterior-position">Mechanism of Left Mento-Anterior Position<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mechanism-of-left-mento-anterior-position" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>In face presentation, you will be substituting occiput with the chin. Instead of flexion you will maintain deflexion and instead of extension you will maintain flexion. Now look at the secret formula:</p>
<ul>
<li>Lie is longitudinal</li>
<li>Attitude is one of extension of the head and the back</li>
<li>The presentation is face</li>
<li>The position is left mento anterior. In a left mento anterior position the orbital ridges will be in the left oblique diameter of the pelvis</li>
<li>The denominator is the mentum</li>
<li>The presenting part is the left molar bone</li>
</ul>
