<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="extension">Extension<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#extension" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Descent takes place throughout and with increasing extension and thus the mentum becomes the leading part</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="internal-rotation-of-the-head">Internal Rotation of the Head<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#internal-rotation-of-the-head" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>This occurs when the chin reaches the pelvis floor and rotates forwards 1/8 of a circle. The chin escapes under the symphysis pubis. When this takes place and the sinciput, vertex and occiput sweep the perineum, the head is born.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="restitution">Restitution<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#restitution" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>This occurs when the chin turns 1/8 of a circle to the mother's left.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="internal-rotation-of-shoulders">Internal Rotation of Shoulders<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#internal-rotation-of-shoulders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The shoulders enter the pelvis in the left oblique diameter and the anterior shoulder reaches the pelvis floor first and rotates forward 1/8 of a circle along the right side of the pelvis.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="external-rotation-of-the-head">External Rotation of the Head<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#external-rotation-of-the-head" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>This occurs simultaneously and the chin moves a further 1/8 of a circle to the left.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="lateral-flexion">Lateral Flexion<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#lateral-flexion" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The anterior shoulder escapes under the symphysis pubis, the posterior shoulder sweeps the perineum and the body is born by a movement of lateral flexion.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="prolonged-labour">Prolonged Labour<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prolonged-labour" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Labour is often prolonged due to ineffective uterine contraction caused by an ill-fitting presenting part. The facial bones do not mould and in order to enable the mentum reach the pelvic floor and rotate forwards, the shoulders must enter the pelvic cavity at the same time as the head.</p>
<p>With good uterine contractions, descent and rotation of the head occurs and labour progresses through to a spontaneous delivery.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="mento-posterior-position">Mento-Posterior Position<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mento-posterior-position" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>When the head is completely extended with an effective contraction, the mentum reaches the pelvic floor first and will rotate forwards an the position becomes anterior.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="persistent-mento-posterior-position">Persistent Mento-Posterior Position<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#persistent-mento-posterior-position" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The head is incompletely extended, the sinciput reaches the pelvic floor first and rotates forwards 1/8 of a circle, which brings the chin into the hollow of the sacrum. Further mechanism is prohibited, which results in impacted face. In order for further descent, both head and chest have to be accommodated in the pelvis.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management-of-labour-in-face-presentation">Management of Labour in Face Presentation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-labour-in-face-presentation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Upon diagnosing the condition the first action you must take is to inform the doctor about the face presentation. Routine maternal and foetal condition observations are done as in normal labour (maternal pulse, foetal heart rate and contraction) half hourly. Blood pressure and temperature is done two hourly. Empty the urinary bladder every two hours.</p>
<p>Vaginal examination to determine cervical dilation and descent of the head, is done every four hours to monitor progress of labour. Take care not to injure the foetal eyes. In mento-posterior positions, the midwife should note whether the mentum is lower than the sinciput since rotation and descent depends on this. If the head remains high despite good uterine contractions, the mother is prepared for caesarean section.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management-of-labour-in-face-presentation">Management of Labour in Face Presentation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-labour-in-face-presentation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Face extends to the Perineum</p>
<p>When the face extends to the perineum, give episiotomy to prevent extensive perineum tear.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="face-appears-at-the-vulva">Face appears at the Vulva<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#face-appears-at-the-vulva" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>When the face appears at the vulva, maintain extension by holding back the sinciput until the chin is delivered.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260112-cfef9d54.jpeg" alt="img-12.jpeg">
The baby's face appears at the vulva</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="chin-has-been-delivered">Chin has been delivered<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#chin-has-been-delivered" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Once the chin has been delivered allow the occiput to sweep the perineum. In this way the submento-vertical diameter (11.5cm) distends the vaginal orifice, instead of the mento vertical diameter (13.5cm).</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260112-5375a6d4.jpeg" alt="img-13.jpeg">
The baby's chin has been delivered</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260112-b76e322b.jpeg" alt="img-14.jpeg">
Occiput rides over Perineum
The occiput is allowed to ride over the perineum</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="head-is-flexed-completely">Head is flexed completely<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#head-is-flexed-completely" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The head is flexed completely and it is delivered. Inform the doctor if the head does not descend in the second stage. In a mento-anterior position, it may be possible to deliver the baby using forceps.</p>
<p>If the head becomes impacted, or there is any suspicion of disproportion, a caesarean section will be necessary.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260112-398c054b.jpeg" alt="img-15.jpeg">
The head delivered</p>
<p>There are several possible complications during labour with a face presentation.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="obstructed-labour">Obstructed Labour<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#obstructed-labour" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A minor degree of contracted pelvis may result in obstructed labour as facial bones do not mould. Caesarean section is necessary in persistent mento posterior position.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="cord-prolapse">Cord Prolapse<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cord-prolapse" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A prolapsed cord is more common when the membranes rupture because the face is an ill-fitting presenting part. Always perform a vaginal examination following rupture of membranes to rule out cord prolapse.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="facial-bruising">Facial Bruising<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#facial-bruising" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The baby's head is elongated with a swollen bruised face, oedematous eyelids and lips at birth. You should take great care while performing vaginal examination to avoid injury.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="cerebral-haemorrhage">Cerebral Haemorrhage<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cerebral-haemorrhage" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The lack of moulding of facial bones can lead to intra-cranial haemorrhage caused by excessive compression of the foetal skull or by upward compression in the typical moulding of the foetal skull found in this type of presentation.</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="maternal-trauma">Maternal Trauma<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#maternal-trauma" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Extensive perineal laceration may occur at delivery due to the large submento vertical and bi-parental diameters distending the vagina and perineum. This increases the incidence of caesarean section, which can increase chances of maternal morbidity and mortality.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="breech-presentation">Breech Presentation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#breech-presentation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Breech presentation occurs in about three percent of labour (Campbell &amp; Lees, 2000). Due to the high risks to both the mother and the baby, the present practice is to book all mothers with breech presentation for caesarean section. In breech presentation, the foetus lies with the buttocks in the lower pole of the uterus, after 34 weeks of pregnancy. There is no obvious reason as to why the foetus presents as breech at term but the following points are contributing factors:</p>
<ul>
<li>Maternal causes include contracted pelvis, polyhydramnios and multiple pregnancy</li>
<li>Foetal causes include pre-term labour, hydrocephalus, extended legs</li>
</ul>
<p>Breech presentations are classified as follows:</p>
<ul>
<li>Complete breech; the buttocks presents with the feet and legs flexed on the thighs and the thighs flexed on the abdomen.</li>
<li>Frank breech; the buttocks present with the hips flexed and the legs extended against the abdomen and chest; this is the most common type of breech presentation.</li>
<li>Incomplete breech; one or both feet or the knees extend below the buttocks. This is also known as single or double footling presentation.</li>
<li>Compound breech; the buttocks present with another part such as a hand. This type of presentation is rare.</li>
</ul>
<p>The condition can be diagnosed in the following manner:</p>
<ul>
<li>Previous history of breech, though this is not conclusive</li>
<li>On palpation at the fundus, a round, hard, ballotable mass is palpated</li>
<li>On auscultation, the foetal heart is heard above the level of the umbilicus</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="pre-natal-management-of-breech-presentation">Pre-Natal Management of Breech Presentation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pre-natal-management-of-breech-presentation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The midwife refers the mother to a doctor at thirty two weeks if the breech presentation persists. An x-ray may be done should there be any doubts in diagnosis. It may reveal the following:</p>
<ul>
<li>Shape and size of the pelvis</li>
<li>Size of foetus</li>
<li>Foetal abnormalities, for example; hydrocephaly</li>
<li>Whether the legs are extended or flexed</li>
</ul>
<p>High risk conditions for breech pregnancies include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Multiple pregnancy</li>
<li>Previous scar</li>
<li>Rhesus â€“ve mother</li>
<li>High blood pressure</li>
</ul>
<p>Breech labour may be as easy as normal labour. You will now look at the dangers of breech delivery and how you may prevent them.</p>
<p>Prenatal mortality rate is 10%, while 50% of stillbirths in breech presentation are pre-term. The danger is great, except in the hands of experts. When nearing the second stage of delivery you should:</p>
<ul>
<li>Prepare the equipment for delivery</li>
<li>Prepare resuscitation trolley and drugs in case of an asphyxiated baby</li>
<li>Inform the obstetrician and paediatrician</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="risks-to-the-skull">Risks to the skull<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#risks-to-the-skull" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The soft skull bones are damaged easily. A large skull may be trapped by the partially dilated cervix, which had allowed the other part of the baby to pass through. It is important to make sure the patient does not push prematurely. Use of sedatives can help to keep the mother calm.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="intracranial-haemorrhage">Intracranial haemorrhage<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#intracranial-haemorrhage" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>This may occur due to rapid compression of the unmoulded skull. Venous congestion, which is caused by hypoxia, might occur. It may also result</p>
<p>from the upward force of foetal blood into the intracranial venous sinuses, the sudden release of the head from the cervix and/or the quick extraction process.</p>
<p>This is why it is important to inform the mother as soon as the condition is diagnosed that there may come a time when she will feel that the head is pushing out and she has the urge of</p>
<p>pushing but she should plan to release the head slowly to prevent damage to the baby's head.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="hypoxia">Hypoxia<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hypoxia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is caused by interference with the uteroplacental circulation. You should not use fundal pressure if there is placental separation while the head is still in the vagina.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="cord-compression">Cord compression<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cord-compression" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is inevitable with a big baby, but you can assist by pulling a loop of cord after the baby is born up to the umbilical and try to position it so that it is not nipped. When the cord is compressed, the foetus will be stimulated to prematurely breathe and inhale mucous or liquor which will cause asphyxia at birth and subsequent pneumonia.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="injuries">Injuries<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#injuries" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>It is very easy for the baby to sustain fractures of the lower and upper limbs but you can prevent this by being competent in the delivery of extended legs. You can flex the knee and gradually pull it out. You may also use Lovset's manoeuvre and should know how to splint the upper arm and flex the elbow.</p>
<p>Prevent rupture of the liver and spleen by holding the baby at the iliac crest with the thumbs at the sacrum. Avoid holding the baby at the kidney level to prevent damage to adrenals. Paralysis can occur due to crushing of the spinal cord. To prevent crushing the spinal cord you, should always check that the sub occipital area appears before you carry an upward traction.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="mechanism-of-labour-in-a-left-sacro-anterior-lsa-position">Mechanism of Labour in a Left Sacro Anterior (LSA) Position<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mechanism-of-labour-in-a-left-sacro-anterior-lsa-position" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The bitrochanteric diameter (10cm) enters in the left oblique diameter of the pelvic brim. The sacrum points to the left ilio-pectineal eminence.</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Summary of LSA Position</th><th></th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Position</td><td>Left â€“ Left Sacro-Anterior, LSA</td></tr><tr><td>Lie</td><td>Longitudinal</td></tr><tr><td>Attitude</td><td>Complete flexion</td></tr><tr><td>Presentation</td><td>Breech</td></tr><tr><td>Denominator</td><td>Sacrum</td></tr><tr><td>Presenting part</td><td>Anterior buttock</td></tr></tbody></table>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="descent">Descent<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#descent" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This takes place with increasing compaction due to increased flexion of limbs.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="internal-rotation-of-the-buttocks">Internal Rotation of the Buttocks<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#internal-rotation-of-the-buttocks" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The anterior buttock reaches the pelvic floor first and rotates one eighth of a circle forwards along the right side of pelvis. The bitrochanteric diameter is now in the antero-posterior diameter of the outlet.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="lateral-flexion-of-the-body">Lateral Flexion of the Body<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#lateral-flexion-of-the-body" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The anterior buttock escapes under the symphysis pubis. The posterior buttock sweeps the perineum and the buttocks are born by a movement of lateral flexion.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="restitution-of-the-buttock">Restitution of the Buttock<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#restitution-of-the-buttock" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The anterior buttock turns slightly to the patient's right side.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="internal-rotation-of-the-shoulders">Internal Rotation of the Shoulders<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#internal-rotation-of-the-shoulders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The shoulders enter in the same oblique diameter of the brim as the buttocks. The anterior shoulder rotates forwards one eighth of a circle along the right side of the pelvis and escapes under the symphysis pubis. The posterior shoulder sweeps the perineum and the shoulders are born.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="internal-rotation-of-the-head">Internal Rotation of the Head<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#internal-rotation-of-the-head" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The head enters in the transverse diameter of the pelvic brim. The occiput rotates along the left or right side of the pelvis. The sub-occipital region (nape of the neck) impinges under surface of the symphysis pubis.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="external-rotation-of-the-body">External Rotation of the Body<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#external-rotation-of-the-body" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The body turns so that the back is uppermost, a movement which accompanies internal rotation of the head.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="birth-of-the-head">Birth of the Head<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#birth-of-the-head" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The chin, face and sinciput sweep the perineum and the head is born in flexed attitude.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="second-stage-of-labour">Second Stage of Labour<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#second-stage-of-labour" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>At this stage you should reassure the mother and confirm fully dilation of the cervix by performing vaginal examination.</p>
<p><strong>Note:</strong></p>
<p>You should not be overly concerned by seeing the buttocks at the vulva as they are soft and can pass through a 6cm dilated os.</p>
<p>Delivery of Complete Breech</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>The following procedure should be followed when delivering the complete breech:</p>
<ul>
<li>Mother's buttocks are positioned at the edge of the bed to allow the baby to hang and apply supra-pubic pressure to the head if required</li>
<li>Give episiotomy when the buttocks extend the perineum, to avoid compression of a moulded head</li>
<li>The buttocks should be expelled by an aided bearing down effort of the mother</li>
<li>With the same contraction the baby is born up to the umbilicus</li>
<li>Pull a loop of cord to prevent traction of the cord. The cord should be handled gently to avoid inducing spasm and should be nipped under the pubic arch to avoid anoxia</li>
<li>Check if elbows are on the chest as is the case with complete breech</li>
<li>The midwife can assist the expulsion of the shoulder by wrapping a small towel around the baby's hips as it is slippery and loses heat</li>
<li>Hold the baby by the iliac crest to avoid crushing of liver and spleen</li>
</ul>
<p>The key point to remember is: 'Hands off the breech! Let nature take its course!'</p>
<p>The procedure continues:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>While the uterus is contracting and the woman pushing, the anterior shoulder escapes under the symphysis pubis</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Elevate the buttocks to allow the posterior shoulder to sweep the perineum</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The back should be in the uppermost position until the shoulders are born</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>As soon as the shoulders are born, let the baby hang by its weight for one or two minutes</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>When the hairline appears, grasp the baby by the feet and hold the stretch, applying sufficient traction to prevent fracture of the neck</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Move the feet through an arch of 180Â° until the mouth and nose are free at the vulva</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>You are now holding the baby upside down and mechanical suction can be used to clear the airway to avoid asphyxia</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>At this stage, ask the mother to pant through an open mouth, 'breathing out the head'. One or two minutes should elapse to allow slow delivery of the vault of the head to prevent a tentorial tear</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260112-a4796b52.jpeg" alt="img-16.jpeg">
Delivery of the head (The Burns Marshall method)</p>
<p>The previous pages describe a routine complete breech delivery where the apgar score is usually about seven to eight. The breech delivery, however, may not always be this simple. This is supposed to be a doctor's procedure but many times you may have to perform it and perform it efficiently. Should you be called upon to assist in the management of extended legs, you should follow this procedure:</p>
<ul>
<li>Apply downward traction until popliteal fossae appear at the vulva</li>
<li>An episiotomy is made when the buttocks extend the perineum</li>
<li>Pressure is applied at the popliteal fossae with abduction of the thigh</li>
<li>The knee will flex and this will aid extraction of the feet and avoid fractures of lower limbs</li>
</ul>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<ul>
<li>The foot will be swept over the baby's abdomen and the feet are born</li>
<li>You should now wait until the baby is delivered up to the umbilicus, pull a loop of cord</li>
<li>Feel for the elbow at the chest, which should not be felt with extended hands</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260112-2da36f64.jpeg" alt="img-17.jpeg">
Management of the extended legs</p>
<p>In a situation where you are called upon to aid with the delivery of the extended hands, you should apply the Lovset manoeuvre. This is a combination of rotation and downward traction to deliver the arms whatever position they are in. The direction of rotation must always bring the back uppermost. When the baby's umbilicus is born and shoulders are in antero-posterior diameter, grasp the baby by the iliac crest applying downward traction until the axilla is visible. Rotate the baby through half a circle 180Â° anticlockwise. One arm which is now anterior is delivered. Rotate the baby back 180Â° clockwise and the second shoulder is delivered in a similar manner. Please refer to Myles, Margaret Text book of Midwives for a complete demonstration of this process.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="take-hold-of-the-baby">Take hold of the baby<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#take-hold-of-the-baby" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The position of the baby is Left Sacro-Anterior. During a contraction when the umbilicus is born and the shoulders are in the anteroposterior diameter, grasp the baby at the iliac crest with the thumbs over the sacrum. A small towel should be wrapped around the baby's waist to prevent it from being slippery.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260112-4efdcce1.jpeg" alt="img-18.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="rotate-the-baby">Rotate the baby<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#rotate-the-baby" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Rotate the baby through half a circle, 180Â° anticlockwise, (starting by turning the back uppermost) while applying downwards traction until the axillar is visible. The hand that was posterior now becomes anterior, this movement sweeps the arm in front of the face and also allows the shoulders to enter the pelvis in the transverse diameter.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260112-722ed183.jpeg" alt="img-19.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="deliver-the-anterior-arm">Deliver the anterior arm<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#deliver-the-anterior-arm" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The arm that was previously posterior is now anterior. With the two first fingers of your left hand (which is at the baby's back) splint the baby's humerous to avoid breaking it.</p>
<p>The elbow is drawn downwards and delivered under the pubic arch. Wait for the next contraction.</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 179 of 317
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260112-f9341ee1.jpeg" alt="img-20.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="rotate-the-baby-again">Rotate the baby again<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#rotate-the-baby-again" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Rotating the body half circle clockwise, make anterior arm posterior. Using the right hand, splint the humerous, draw it downwards and deliver it under the pubic arch.</p>
<p>Repeat the next side and deliver the other hand.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260112-7152b16a.jpeg" alt="img-21.jpeg"></p>
<p>It sounds easy, but you will agree that at times applying tractions can be a very arduous task. Now look at the diagram of how you will position your hands and fingers when performing the Mauriceau-Smellie-Veit Manoeuvre (jaw flexion and shoulder traction).</p>
<p>The following procedure should be followed when delivering the extended head:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Position hands and fingers to extract extended head</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Put the baby astride your left arm with the palm supporting the chest</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>First and third finger of left hand should be placed on the malar bones to flex the head, middle finger in the mouth well back to aid flexion</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>First and second right hand fingers should be hooked over the shoulders pulling moderately in a downwards direction</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260112-c1733e49.jpeg" alt="img-22.jpeg">
Delivery of the extended head (Mauriceau-Smellie-Veit Manoeuvre)</p>
<p>The procedure continues:</p>
<ul>
<li>Controlled traction is exerted in a downwards direction as the head descends in the curved birth canal. Traction continues until the sub occiput area appears before the appearance of the nape of the neck. Upward traction at this level will inflict fracture of the neck</li>
<li>Instruct the mother to pant</li>
<li>Exert traction in upward direction to allow for the birth of the head. Nose and mouth are free. Your intervention will clear the airway</li>
<li>The Vault is delivered slowly</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="causes-of-delayed-breech">Causes of Delayed Breech<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causes-of-delayed-breech" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The following are some of the causes of delayed breech:</p>
<ul>
<li>Delay in the first stage is rare, though it may be caused by impaction due to a large baby, a small pelvis or weak contractions in which case a caesarean section is done</li>
<li>Delay during the second stage is usually caused by extended legs</li>
</ul>
<p>In terms of management, nothing should be done until the buttocks extend the perineum. At this point you should perform a medio-lateral episiotomy.</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 180 of 317
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>Delay in the Birth of the Head</p>
<p>If an insufficiently dilated cervix holds up the head, the baby will make gasping movements. You should mop the vaginal wall in contact with the baby's face and inserting two fingers make a channel through which you can meet the baby. If the head is arrested high in the cavity, disproportion may exist. Suprapubic pressure may help, but application of forceps is necessary. The doctor will use forceps for the delivery of the coming head.</p>
<p>SECTION 4: ABNORMAL PUERPERIUM</p>
<p>Introduction</p>
<p>You are now going to look at abnormal purperium. First you need to reflect on the meaning of the puerperium or postpartum period.</p>
<p>The puerperium or postpartum period starts about one hour after delivery and continues for the next six weeks. During the postpartum period, the mother goes through physical and psychological transition caused by what she has gone through her pregnancy with all the adjustments of hormones, not to mention the stress and fatigue of labour. Her body is vulnerable to many complications due to blood loss, laceration and injury of the birth canal.</p>
<p>Complications during this period are associated with trauma sustained during childbirth, disorders of the circulatory system or psychological disorders. Postpartum nursing starts from early pregnancy. At that time it is important to prevent the occurrence of complications by treating all infections and controlling chronic diseases from getting worse. Give health education to maintain cleanliness and physical status by encouraging balanced diet to prevent anaemia. During labour, aseptic techniques and vigilant observation should be used to enable early detections of complications that are likely to arise. This will allow you to take appropriate action in good time. During the postpartum period, provide appropriate care and counselling to prevent anxiety, and ensure that the new mother has enough rest and sleep. Try keeping the stressed mother calm. Observe her closely to detect any early signs of complications and treat them promptly.</p>
<p>Objectives</p>
<p>By the end of this section you will be able to:</p>
<ul>
<li>Define puerperal pyrexia</li>
<li>Describe the management of puerperal pyrexia</li>
<li>Define various breast conditions</li>
<li>Explain the management of breast complications during puerperium</li>
</ul>
<p>Puerperal Pyrexia</p>
<p>Puerperal pyrexia is a febrile condition, which presents with a temperature of 38Â°C and above within 14 - 21 days following childbirth or abortion.</p>
<p>Causes of puerperal pyrexia include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Genital tract infection</li>
<li>Urinary tract infection</li>
<li>Breast disorders, for example, mastitis, breast engorgement or breast abscess</li>
<li>Thrombophlebitis</li>
<li>Respiratory tract infection</li>
<li>Other causes of pyrexia such as malaria</li>
<li>Vesico-vaginal fistula</li>
<li>Recto-vaginal fistula</li>
<li>Pyrexia of unknown origin</li>
</ul>
<p>After separation of the placenta, a superficial wound is left on the uterine wall. Other wounds may be present on the birth canal, depending on the type of delivery. These wounds may be minor bruises or deep tears of the cervix, vagina or perineum. If not appropriately managed, puerperal pyrexia ensues.</p>
<p>Bacteriology</p>
<p>Bacterial organisms are classified in two groups: Endogenous and Exogenous.</p>
<p>Endogenous Organisms</p>
<p>These are harmless organisms, which are present in the lower intestinal tract, on the perineum and in the vagina. They have a role to play in the ecology of the body. Escherichia coli inhabit the bowel and the vagina. Streptococcus faecalis reside in the lower intestine and the anus. Anaerobic streptococci and Clostridium welchii are found in the vagina.</p>
<p>Exogenous Organisms</p>
<p>These are imported into the birth canal from other sources such as the hands of birth attendants or airborne infections from other patients or visitors. The organisms are harboured in dust and in the throat.</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>Staphylococcus aureus is the main cause of breast infection found in dust and has developed resistance to antibiotics in recent years.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="pathology">Pathology<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pathology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>When the organisms enter the tissues, the whole process depends on:</p>
<ul>
<li>The virulence of the organisms</li>
<li>The body's ability to resist invasion (strength of immune system)</li>
<li>The trauma inflicted to tissues</li>
<li>The effectiveness of the antibiotic and the time of commencement</li>
</ul>
<p>The first sign of genital tract infection is pyrexia with a rising pulse rate 24 hours or more after delivery.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="puerperal-sepsis">Puerperal Sepsis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#puerperal-sepsis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is an infection of the genital tract occurring any time between rupture of membranes or labour and six weeks after delivery or abortion. Two or more of the following will be present; pelvic pain, fever, abnormal vaginal discharge, abnormal smell, foul odorous discharge and delay to uteral restitution. There are three types of puerperal sepsis: mild, moderate and severe.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="mild-infection">Mild infection<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mild-infection" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The infection is usually localised to the specific tissues of the area, for example, the vagina, cervix or uterus. The temperature is gradually stepped up but rarely goes beyond 38Â°C. The mother may have no other complications or symptoms. With prompt appropriate antibiotic use, the condition should be cured within three to four days.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="moderate-infection">Moderate infection<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#moderate-infection" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>When endometritis develops, it manifests in about 48 to 72 hours after delivery. The mother complains of loss of appetite, headache, backache and general discomfort. The pulse rate ranges from 100 - 120mmHg. The temperature is rarely above 38.8Â°C. The uterus is bulky and tender to the touch. Lochia discharge may decrease in amount. It is a red brownish colour and has a foul smell.</p>
<p>In cases of Haemolytic streptococcus, the lochia may be odourless initially. If the infection is contained in the endometrium, it clears within seven to ten days of treatment.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="severe-infection">Severe infection<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#severe-infection" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The virulent strain of haemolytic streptococcus rapidly infects the entire peritoneal cavity and causes septicaemia and haemolytic anaemia by gaining access to the circulatory system through the placental site. The mother will have a persistent fever of over 39Â°C, which may be continuous or remittent. Rigours are common and the pulse usually ranges from 140 - 160mmHg.</p>
<p>The uterus is sub-involuted and tender to the touch. Pallor is marked due to anaemia. There is persistent vomiting and sometimes diarrhoea. The mother appears very sick, restless and complains of insomnia.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="diagnostic-physical-examination">Diagnostic Physical Examination<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnostic-physical-examination" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The following procedure should be followed when conducting a diagnostic examination:</p>
<ul>
<li>Head to toe examination should be done.</li>
<li>Check on mucous membranes for pallor, throat for infection, breast for engorgement or swollen glands and abdomen for tenderness.</li>
<li>Check the uterus for sub involution, and the perineum for any signs of infection from tears and episiotomy.</li>
<li>Inspect the legs for any inflammation.</li>
</ul>
<p>When carrying out investigations, the following steps should be taken:</p>
<ul>
<li>Take a high vaginal swab. The use of a speculum may be difficult, and no antiseptic solution or cream should be used to lubricate the speculum. Use aseptic technique.</li>
<li>Sample blood for haemogram, WBC total and differential.</li>
<li>In very serious cases blood culture is done.</li>
<li>High vaginal swab for culture and sensitivity.</li>
<li>Sample mid-stream urine for culture and sensitivity.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="medical-treatment">Medical Treatment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#medical-treatment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The following methods may be used to treat the condition:</p>
<ul>
<li>A broad spectrum antibiotic is given soon after the collection of vaginal and urine specimen to be changed when the result of high vaginal swab is ready.</li>
<li>An analgesic in case of pain, and a sedative to ensure good sleep, is commenced.</li>
<li>The mother should be placed on iron supplements if not on them already.</li>
<li>If haemoglobin is below 7.4dl packed cell transfusion is recommended.</li>
</ul>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 182 of 317
Bishop's Computers</p>
<ul>
<li>Fluid and electrolytes balances should be ensured on a daily basis. In case of imbalance, 5% glucose infusion with added vitamins and potassium chloride is given.</li>
<li>In case of infected perineal wound, the stitch should be clipped to allow drainage of pus.</li>
<li>Localised infection is treated, with hydrogen peroxide and antibiotic spray.</li>
<li>It may be necessary at times to incise and drain a pelvic abscess made through posterior vaginal fornix or rectum.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="nursing-care">Nursing Care<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-care" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>You will now look at what kind of care should be provided to the mother. Isolate her until the cause has been identified, antibiotics started and the temperature has settled. Unless the mother is severely ill, the baby stays with her and the midwife will help her take care of the baby. Try to keep the mother free of stress and exhaustion.</p>
<p>You should nurse the mother in a propped up position with a pillow to encourage uterine drainage of lochia. Adoption of prone position for half an hour will also serve the same. Encourage the mother to eat a light nutritious diet, ensuring she takes plenty of fluids. You should reserve a bathtub for her use only if she is able to go to the bathroom.</p>
<p>She should have vulva swabs every four hours and change of beddings frequently. You should also check her pulse rate and blood pressure every four hours and carry out a daily head to toe examination to assess her condition.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="prevention-of-post-partum-infection">Prevention of Post Partum Infection<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prevention-of-post-partum-infection" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The mother should be advised to eat a well balanced diet before and during pregnancy to prevent anaemia. She should receive early and regular prenatal care and exercise moderately, which will promote good health during pregnancy.</p>
<p>In the hospital, ensure proper infection control and monitoring, for example, cultures in the ward and nasal pharyngeal cultures from the personnel. Maintain the use of the aseptic technique. You will be able to minimise the risk of haemorrhage by proper management of the three stages of labour. Finally, you should try to prevent caesarean section whenever possible.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="breast-disorders-during-the-puerperal-period">Breast Disorders During the Puerperal Period<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#breast-disorders-during-the-puerperal-period" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Breast disorders may affect the whole breast or the nipples.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="engagement-of-the-breast">Engagement of the Breast<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#engagement-of-the-breast" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>On the third day postpartum secretion of milk begins. If the baby does not empty the breast it becomes over distended. The breast becomes enlarged and covered with distended veins, which are tender, hard and knotty. The mother may also have palpable nodules in the axilla and will experience sleepless nights due to pain.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="treatment-of-engorged-breasts">Treatment of Engorged Breasts<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#treatment-of-engorged-breasts" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In the early stages of engorgement, the breast may be emptied by manual expressing to relieve congestion. In the latter stage, the congestion and pressure of the ducts prevents the flow of milk. Manual expression of the breast should be done to promote flow of breast milk before the baby is fixed on the breast. When the mother cannot tolerate manual expression, electrical or manual breast pump should be used. You should administer an analgesic and ensure that the mother's breasts are effectively supported by a well-fitting, lactating bra.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="cracked-nipple">Cracked Nipple<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cracked-nipple" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Sore nipples are caused by either the loss of the epithelium cover on a big area of the nipple or a deep, small, painful crack at either the tip or base of the nipple. The two conditions may also exist simultaneously. There are several reasons why cracked nipples may occur. These include:</p>
<ul>
<li>A flat nipple (try to pull it at 37 weeks to prevent infection and premature labour)</li>
<li>Wet and unhygienic nipple</li>
<li>Badly fixed baby on the breast covering the baby's nostrils</li>
<li>Leaving the baby too long on the breast</li>
<li>Untoughened breast during pregnancy</li>
</ul>
<p>Certain complications may arise from this condition. There is a risk of formation of abscess as the ducts are not emptied and as a result of the raw area which allows access for micro-organisms.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="recommended-methods-of-treatment-for-cracked-nipples">Recommended Methods of Treatment for Cracked Nipples<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#recommended-methods-of-treatment-for-cracked-nipples" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Rest the breast for 24 hours or until the crack is healed</li>
<li>Meanwhile express the milk manually</li>
</ul>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<ul>
<li>Expose the breast to the air for 20 minutes six hourly or to an electric lamp 30cm distance to promote healing</li>
<li>Apply lanoline or massage cream ointment for soothing the nipple</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="acute-puerperal-mastitis">Acute Puerperal Mastitis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#acute-puerperal-mastitis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Mastitis is the inflammation of the breast. If the condition is not treated, it may proceed to abscess formation. The term 'flushed breast' is applied in mild cases where the infection is superficial and localised. The condition rarely occurs prior to the eighth day of puerperium. It commonly arises during the second or third week. Mastitis may arise in two different ways. Cellulitis infection occurs when the infectious micro-organism enters through the cracked nipple and spreads through the interlobular tissue. Adenitis is a result of the multiplication of organisms which are already present in the breast itself due to engorgement, static of milk or bruising through careless handling.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="primary-causative-organisms-of-mastitis">Primary Causative Organisms of Mastitis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#primary-causative-organisms-of-mastitis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The primary causative organisms are streptococcus i.e. haemolytic streptococcus organisms and staphylococcus aureus. The usual route for transmission of organisms to the mother's breast is from the:</p>
<ul>
<li>Nasopharynx of her infant</li>
<li>The patient's hands</li>
<li>Nursery personnel in contact with the infant</li>
<li>Skin infection of the baby</li>
<li>The umbilical cord</li>
</ul>
<p>The main signs and symptoms of the condition are:</p>
<ul>
<li>The mother complains of acute pain and tenderness in the breast</li>
<li>General malaise characterised by a chilly sensation, followed by rise of temperature to 40Â°C with increased pulse rate</li>
<li>On inspection, the breast appears reddened and hard</li>
<li>The inflammation may be generalised, confined to a lobe or a local area</li>
<li>There are indurations, tenderness and erythema of the involved area</li>
<li>Mastitis is usually unilateral, in advanced cases there maybe local abscess formation</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management-of-mastitis">Management of Mastitis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-mastitis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A sample of breast milk should be taken for bacteriological examination. Broad spectrum antibiotics should be administered immediately while awaiting the culture result. Depending upon virulence and resistance, cephalosporin or vancomycin drugs that are particularly effective against staphylococcal infections should be administered to prevent formation of breast abscess.</p>
<p>As soon as mastitis occurs, breast feeding on the affected area should be suspended. Empty the breast by gentle expression or with an electric breast pump. Support the breast with a firm breast binder or a well fitted brassiere. Heat application may be ordered to hasten the localisation of the abscess.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="abscess-of-the-breast">Abscess of the Breast<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#abscess-of-the-breast" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Acute mastitis may lead to a mammary abscess. Part of the breast becomes painful, tender, and oedematous with redness of the overlying skin. The axillary's glands become tender and enlarged. The abscess may form near the surface or in the substance of the breast. If untreated, a deep abscess may burrow in several directions affecting the whole breast.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="treatments-for-abscesses-of-the-breast">Treatments for Abscesses of the Breast<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#treatments-for-abscesses-of-the-breast" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Treatments include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Lactation is suppressed with Bromocriptine (2.5mg) twice for 14 days</li>
<li>A radical incision is made externally from near the areola margin towards the perineal of the breast</li>
<li>Avoid cutting the lactiferous ducts. Insert gauze drainage after you evacuate the pus</li>
<li>Post-operative care is the same as for any surgical patient</li>
</ul>
<p>In the case of breast abscess, there is need for urgent suppression of lactation. Bromocriptine (2.5mg BD) is given for 14 days, although it should be noted that this treatment is expensive. However, it is preferred to oestrogen due to the risk of varicose thrombosis with the latter. In many cases all that is needed is supporting the breasts firmly and limiting fluid intake.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="prevention-of-breast-complications">Prevention of Breast Complications<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prevention-of-breast-complications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Encourage breastfeeding by providing information on the advantage of breastfeeding. Educate the mother during prenatal care on the prevention of breast complications. Help her to fix the baby properly on the breast. Stress the</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>importance of emptying the breast by manual expression in case of excess milk, to avoid engorgement. You should also emphasise the importance of infection prevention, including prompt treatment of any members of the family with boils, burns or any skin lesions.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="extra-genital-infection">Extra Genital Infection<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#extra-genital-infection" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="urinary-tract-infection">Urinary Tract Infection<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#urinary-tract-infection" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Pyelonephritis occurs in a number of cases during the puerperium. Proper treatment during pregnancy will prevent recurrence of the condition. For more information regarding urinary tract infections, refer to unit five.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="respiratory-infection">Respiratory Infection<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#respiratory-infection" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>A respiratory infection may cause puerperal pyrexia. The possibility of sepsis must be ruled out; otherwise both conditions may be present at the same time. For more information on respiratory management, see unit five.</p>
