<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="venous-thrombosis">Venous Thrombosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#venous-thrombosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This refers to the formation of clots in the veins, usually in the lower limbs. Puerperal mothers are prone to venous thrombosis. Puerperal mothers who have had a caesarean section often haemorrhage and after a difficult delivery it may take a longer time for her to move around. Another possible cause of the condition is varicosity, which may occur during delivery due to injury or inflammation. Mothers over 35 years and those with high parity are also at high risk.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="prophylaxis">Prophylaxis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prophylaxis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>During pregnancy you should ensure that pregnant mothers with thrombo-embolic disorders are not given oestrogen preparations and are encouraged to do exercise. Pregnant women with marked varicose veins should wear embolic stockings or crepe bandage. Mothers at a high risk of developing thrombosis or pulmonary embolism should be given a low dose of heparin 5,000 units subcutaneous.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="section-5-obstetric-anaesthesia-operations-and-emergencies">SECTION 5: OBSTETRIC ANAESTHESIA, OPERATIONS AND EMERGENCIES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#section-5-obstetric-anaesthesia-operations-and-emergencies" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="introduction">Introduction<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#introduction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>You are now in the fifth section of this unit on labour. In the previous section you learnt that abnormal labour presents special challenges and carries many risks. This is why you should refer such women to the doctor in the prenatal clinic during their third trimester. They should also be advised to deliver in the hospital, as they may need a caesarean section.</p>
<p>In this section, you will study obstetric anaesthesia, operations and emergencies.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="objectives">Objectives<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#objectives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>By the end of this section you will be able to:</p>
<ul>
<li>Describe obstetric anaesthesia</li>
<li>Describe the management of obstetric operations</li>
<li>Describe the management of obstetric emergencies</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="obstetric-anaesthesia">Obstetric Anaesthesia<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#obstetric-anaesthesia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>By the end of this topic you will be able to:</p>
<ul>
<li>Differentiate between anaesthesia and analgesia</li>
<li>Describe the risks associated with anaesthesia with particular emphasis on how to prevent these risks</li>
<li>Describe the role of a midwife in the administration of anaesthesia</li>
</ul>
<p>Anaesthesia means absence of sensation and freedom from pain. General anaesthesia is the induction of unconsciousness, which may also involve the giving of some analgesia.</p>
<p>Regional anaesthesia is when a group of nerves is made free of sensation. Local anaesthesia is when a specific area of the body is anaesthetised e.g. the perineal area when repairing an episiotomy perineal or vaginal tear. Each of these three categories of anaesthesia will be covered in this topic.</p>
<p><strong>Remember:</strong> General anaesthesia for a pregnant woman in her second and third trimesters, or for a mother who has just delivered, is dangerous due to the effect of progesterone.</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 185 of 317
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 186 of 317
Bishop's Computers</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="general-anaesthesia">General Anaesthesia<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#general-anaesthesia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>It is essential that only trained anaesthesia personnel administer general anaesthesia to patients. Moreover, it is essential to place an endotracheal tube in all pregnant patients undergoing general anaesthesia, since the risk of aspiration pneumonitis, secondary to the inhalation of gastric content, is a significant one.</p>
<p>Until the baby is born, the mother should receive 100% oxygen and a low concentration of an inhalation agent such as isoflurane 0.5%. After delivery anaesthesia can be deepened by supplementing the anaesthetic with higher concentrations of potent volatile inhalation agents.</p>
<p>Factors connected with anaesthesia have been a significant cause of maternal deaths until very recently. It is essential for the midwife to be aware of the risks associated with anaesthesia and why they occur, so as to give intelligent help to assist the operating team and the patient.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="problems-in-obstetrics-anaesthesia">Problems in Obstetrics Anaesthesia<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#problems-in-obstetrics-anaesthesia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>In obstetrics the anaesthetic problems are due to:</p>
<ul>
<li>Effects of progesterone on the mother</li>
<li>The pressure from the gravid uterus</li>
<li>The presence of two patients rather than one patient</li>
</ul>
<p>Some of the problems include; Mendelson's syndrome, failed intubation, aortalcaval occlusion and maternal awareness.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="mendelson-s-syndrome">Mendelson's Syndrome<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mendelson-s-syndrome" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>It is believed that in pregnancy and especially in advanced labour there is a delay in gastric emptying time, due to the effect of progesterone on the gastro-intestinal tract.</p>
<p>Narcotic analgesics like pethidine that are given in labour, cause significant delay in gastric emptying. The static stomach content raises the pH. Fasting also gives similar reactions. The pressure from the gravid uterus results in the reflux of the contents in the stomach when the mother is in recumbent position. When she is under general anaesthetic unnoticed regurgitation may occur. In cases where the acid stomach contents are aspirated into the lungs, a condition known as Mendelson's Syndrome result. The alveoli are damaged which causes the impairment of gaseous exchange. It is impossible to oxygenate the mother and in severe cases death may ensue.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="prevention-of-mendelson-s-syndrome">Prevention of Mendelson's Syndrome<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prevention-of-mendelson-s-syndrome" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The main method of prevention is the administration of antacid therapy while in labour to high risk patients.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="rapid-sequence-induction">Rapid Sequence Induction<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#rapid-sequence-induction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Rapid sequence induction is used for unprepared patients. Prepared obstetric patients are also liable to have acid contents in the stomach and the same technique is used. The method always includes endo-tracheal intubation with the use of cricoid pressure, which protects the lungs even when silent regurgitation occurs.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cricoid-pressure">Cricoid Pressure<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cricoid-pressure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The cricoid cartilage is pressurised to close the oesophagus, preventing acid reflux. This pressure is essential in preventing the death of the mother. Proper application of cricoid pressure is essential. When intubation fails and the anaesthetist is able to maintain a clear airway, a facemask should be used while the assistant maintains cricoid pressure. Another option is spinal anaesthesia, after waking the mother.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="failed-intubation">Failed Intubation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#failed-intubation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>This usually occurs in pregnant women with laryngeal oedema due to pregnancy and induced hypertension. The anaesthetist has difficulties visualising the vocal cords and introducing the tracheal tube. Other factors include poor opening of the mouth and a stiff or fat neck.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="prevention">Prevention<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prevention" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Use a pre-oxygenation technique, which involves giving facemask oxygen for four minutes uninterrupted. This will prevent cyanosis significantly when attempting to intubate.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="aortocaval-occlusion">Aortocaval occlusion<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#aortocaval-occlusion" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>You will now look at aortocaval occlusion and its prevention. The cause of aortocaval occlusion is the weight of the gravid uterus, which partially blocks the inferior vena cava. The venous return is then reduced, which in turn leads to a fall of cardiac output. This occurs when a pregnant</p>
<p>woman lies supine in late pregnancy for a long period in labour. If an emergency caesarean section is being performed due to foetal distress, aortocaval occlusion increases the foetal distress and causes further foetal hypoxia.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="do-you-know-how-this-might-be-prevented">Do you know how this might be prevented?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#do-you-know-how-this-might-be-prevented" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This condition can be prevented by encouraging the mother in labour to remain in an upright position for as long as possible. During labour, when the woman needs to lie flat, the midwife should ensure she is tilted to the left, either with a small rubber wedge under the mattress or a folded blanket under the left buttock at an angle of 15Â°. Modern delivery beds, chairs and operation tables have this facility incorporated.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="maternal-awareness">Maternal Awareness<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#maternal-awareness" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>While giving general anaesthesia most of the drugs, except muscle relaxants, will pass the placental barrier and result in a sleepy baby. To prevent this, a light anaesthetic agent is given. The woman retains a high level of consciousness and she is able to recall events that occurred during the operation. However, she is unable to give any indication of sensation since she is paralysed. A woman who has retained awareness cannot recall pain but recalls the whole conversation during the operation. This can be a terrifying experience, since she may not want to know what was happening.</p>
<p>Awareness often occurs when nitrous oxide is used alone.</p>
<p>The addition of an opiate intravenously as soon as the baby is delivered is known to reduce maternal awareness significantly. In order to prevent maternal awareness you should maintain neither too deep nor too light a level of anaesthesia for the mother. In this manner, you will also be able to prevent Mendelson's Syndrome, aortocaval occlusion and foetal hypoxia.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="regional-anaesthesia">Regional Anaesthesia<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#regional-anaesthesia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The operational region is made free from pain by infiltrating an anaesthetic drug into the nerves supplying the region. This can be achieved in several ways i.e. epidural block, spinal anaesthesia, pudendal block and para cervical block.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="epidural-block">Epidural Block<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#epidural-block" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Epidural analgesia is described as lumbar or caudal, depending on the site used when approaching the epidural space. This is achieved by infiltrating anaesthetic into the epidural space so that it surrounds the fibres of the specific spinal nerves and anaesthetises them, thereby achieving a selective block. This can be done in two ways:</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="lumbar-epidural-block">Lumbar Epidural Block<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#lumbar-epidural-block" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is the most common approach and there are three different techniques which may be used. The anaesthetic is introduced between lumbar vertebrae two and three, or three and four.</p>
<p>First technique: A single shot epidural refers to the process whereby local anaesthesia is introduced using a Touhy needle, but no catheter is inserted for topping up purposes.</p>
<p>Second technique: Intermittent technique is when a polyethylene or nylon catheter is inserted into the epidural space so that further doses of local anaesthetic may be given when required.</p>
<p>Third technique: The continuous technique is where anaesthetic solution is infused via epidural catheter using an intravenous infusion line attached to an electronic drip counter.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="caudal-epidural-block">Caudal Epidural Block<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#caudal-epidural-block" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is an uncommon technique. The epidural needle is introduced between the sacral vertebra and cocyxiatus through the sacral hiatus.</p>
<p>Contraindications for caudal epidural block include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Maternal reluctance</li>
<li>Bleeding disorders</li>
<li>Systemic or site infection</li>
<li>Existing disease, for example, multiple blood vessels sclerosis</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="regional-anaesthesia">Regional Anaesthesia<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#regional-anaesthesia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>You will now look at some of the indications of epidural analgesia. These include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Request of the mother</li>
<li>Malposition where long, exhausting labour is anticipated</li>
<li>Malpresentation, particularly breech presentation, where an obstetrician requires a well relaxed mother to perform an assisted breech delivery</li>
</ul>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<ul>
<li>Multiple pregnancy where an epidural analgesia is advantageous because it allows for the possibility of manipulative delivery</li>
<li>When the mother is not obtaining adequate pain relief from other analgesic methods and is tense and distressed</li>
</ul>
<p>There are several complications, which may arise from the use of anaesthetics. You will now study each of these in turn.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="complications-of-regional-anaesthesia">Complications of Regional Anaesthesia<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#complications-of-regional-anaesthesia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="hypotension">Hypotension<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hypotension" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>This occurs as a result of the effect of vasodilatation of the blood vessels. Rapid intravenous infusion can prevent the condition. This is commonly known as a preload and commonly consists of between 500ml and 1000ml of Hartman's solution. A functional intravenous infusion is essential before epidural analgesia is commenced in order to prevent hypotension.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="dural-tap">Dural Tap<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#dural-tap" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>This is the accidental puncture of the durameter. This is recognised when a few drops of Cerebrospinal Fluid (CSF) seep through the Tuohy needle. In order to prevent this condition, the anaesthetist normally re-sites the epidural catheter in an adjacent space. The obstetrician is informed and a forceps delivery will be planned in order to prevent the woman from pushing and possibly forcing more CSF through the</p>
<p>dural puncture.</p>
<p>A reduction of CSF volume usually results in severe headache, which resolves spontaneously within a week. Another measure to minimise leakage of CSF is to leave the epidural catheter in position and infuse normal saline with the help of an infusion pump. This is normally continued for 24 hours while the woman is lying flat.</p>
<p>For quick relief of the headache, the anaesthetist may decide to perform a 'blood patch', that is under strict asepsis taking between 10ml - 20ml of venous blood from the woman's antecubital vein and introducing it into the epidural space via the intervertebral space nearest the dural puncture. This results in immediate cure of the headache.</p>
<p>The woman is left to rest for an hour or two to avoid disturbing the clot, which has sealed the</p>
<p>dural puncture. It carries risks of infection but the success rate is 90% on the first occasion and 98% if the procedure is repeated.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="total-spinal-block">Total Spinal Block<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#total-spinal-block" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>This is a rare complication. It occurs when by mistake there is a dural puncture that fails to be recognised and the anaesthetist injects the local anaesthetic solution. This results in rapid motor and sensory block with a drastic fall of blood pressure. The mother collapses and cardiac arrest may follow. If this happens, immediate resuscitation is essential and ventilator support is required.</p>
<p>Occasionally, this effect is seen following a later top up and not during the initial stages of epidural analgesics. The reason for this is unclear but, in some cases, the epidural catheter is thought to have migrated. The midwife who tops up an epidural must be aware of these possible complications and their immediate treatment.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="bloody-tap">Bloody Tap<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#bloody-tap" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>This happens when the anaesthetist punctures one of the epidural veins. Blood is seen in the catheter. In this case the epidural catheter is resited in order to prevent intravenous injection of local anaesthetic solution. If local anaesthetic is injected in the vein, toxicity will result and the woman will complain of tingling or numbness of the mouth and tongue, and dizziness. Her speech may be slurred and she may finally have convulsions.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="patchy-block">Patchy Block<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#patchy-block" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>This is when an epidural block is sometimes more effective on one side of the body or is completely unilateral for no obvious reason. If this occurs the anaesthetist should be informed to adjust the epidural catheter.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="disadvantages-of-local-anaesthesia">Disadvantages of Local Anaesthesia<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#disadvantages-of-local-anaesthesia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>There are several disadvantages of local anaesthetics. These include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Unpleasant experience to the woman who may lose sensation and motor function in her legs</li>
<li>Being unable to pass urine due to unawareness of a full bladder</li>
</ul>
<p>The epidural block may also contribute to the following symptoms in the postnatal period:</p>
<ul>
<li>Impaired bladder function</li>
</ul>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<ul>
<li>Marked perineal pain</li>
<li>Backache due to trauma by the Tuohy needle during the epidural procedure</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="drugs-used-in-epidural-analgesia">Drugs Used in Epidural Analgesia<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#drugs-used-in-epidural-analgesia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>There are several drugs used in epidural analgesia. These are:</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="bupivacaine">Bupivacaine<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#bupivacaine" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>This is administered in strengths of 0.25% and 0.5% and these concentrations are modified as required by diluting with normal saline. It is effective within 10 - 20 minutes of administration and lasts for about two hours during labour. The total dose given is not excessive unless labour is prolonged and toxicity is not common.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="ropivacain-naropin">Ropivacain (Naropin)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ropivacain-naropin" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>This analgesic is good in low concentration with minimal and non-progressive motor block. Its long acting action makes it suitable for use in labour.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="opiates">Opiates<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#opiates" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Drugs in this group include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Diamorphine</li>
<li>Morphine</li>
<li>Pethidine</li>
</ul>
<p>These are good post operative analgesics and neither cause hypotension, nor cause motor or sympathetic block. They are not as effective as might be expected in relieving labour pains but are commonly used in our hospitals following caesarean sections due to the pleasant feeling of wellbeing they induce. There is some risk of respiratory depression, although this risk is minimal.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="lignocaine">Lignocaine<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#lignocaine" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>This is usually administered in the strength of 0.5 - 1% and is one of the more effective local anaesthetics available for epidural administration. The short acting span makes it unsuitable for use through out labour since a large dose may be needed and toxicity is therefore a risk. If the woman is very distressed it may be used for the initial dose and Bupivacaine can be used thereafter.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="spinal-anaesthesia">Spinal Anaesthesia<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#spinal-anaesthesia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Although spinal anaesthesia provides for pain relief at the time of delivery, it is not suitable for use during labour as it decreases the strength of the labour contractions. It is suitable for caesarean section provided the operation is not prolonged beyond the effective time of the anaesthetic solution in use.</p>
<p>A spinal block is performed in a manner similar to an epidural block but in this case a local anaesthestic solution is injected into the subarachnoid space, i.e. in to the cerebrospinal fluid. The woman will have total motor control and sensory block over and below the anaesthetised areas.</p>
<p>There is a greater risk of hypotension with spinal than with epidural block. Blood pressure should be monitored carefully as should the bladder contents.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="pudendal-block">Pudendal Block<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pudendal-block" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Thijs is a technique that is used to anaesthetise areas that are supplied by pudendal nerve, namely lower vargina, perineum and vulva. This method is very unreliable and does not give adequate analgesia.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="para-cervical-block">Para Cervical Block<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#para-cervical-block" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In this technique the para cervical plexus is blocked, this gives pain relief for the first stage of labour but each injection is only effective for about three hours.</p>
<p>The technique is not favourable since the uterine artery passes close to the nerve plexus and inadvertent intra-arterial injection of even a small amount of anaesthesia would lead to foetal bradycardia or intrauterine death.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="local-anaesthesia">Local Anaesthesia<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#local-anaesthesia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Perineal infiltration is very common among midwives who perform it before repairing episiotomies, perineal tears or vaginal tears. Lignocain is commonly used, but there is need for caution as levels above 200ml of 1% solution leads to risk of toxicity.</p>
<p>The midwife should really minimise the risk of intravenous injection, by being observant of the presence of blood in the solution after withdrawing the piston prior to injection.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="inhalation-anaesthesia">Inhalation Anaesthesia<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#inhalation-anaesthesia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is a process by which you administer volatile agents using a facemask in pain relief. It</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>is indicated in the late first stage and during the second stage of labour.</p>
<p>Explain the procedure to the mother to ensure her cooperation. You should let her know that it will relieve the pain. Tell her to breathe in during a contraction and rest during the time the contraction wears off. She has to breathe in for at least 15 to 35 seconds at the beginning of a contraction.</p>
<p>It is contra-indicated under the following circumstances:</p>
<ul>
<li>Antepartum haemorrhage</li>
<li>Preeclampsia</li>
<li>Anaemia</li>
<li>Congestive cardiac failure</li>
<li>In all cases with placental insufficiency</li>
<li>Maternal and foetal distress</li>
<li>Intra uterine growth retardation</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="what-are-the-main-advantages-of-inhalation-anaesthesia">What are the main advantages of inhalation anaesthesia?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-are-the-main-advantages-of-inhalation-anaesthesia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>â˜ It is easy to use
â˜ It can be used by any competent midwife without supervision so long as she knows how to regulate the flow
â˜ Inhalation anaesthesia has shortlived effect on pain relief with no complications to the baby. There are two types of inhalation anaesthesia. These are called:</p>
<ul>
<li>Tritene or trichoboroethylene</li>
<li>Entonox</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="tritene">Tritene<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#tritene" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This has a composition of up to 0.5% of tritene in air. It is blue in colour and a volatile agent. One of the main side effects of this drug is that it accumulates in the maternal blood stream causing sleep but also, at times, disorientation. When this happens you must stop the inhalation. It also accumulates in the foetus, causing drowsiness at birth. It should not be administered for more than four hours. Once the drug is stopped the effect is short lived.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="entonox">Entonox<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#entonox" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This drug is composed of 50% nitrous oxide and 50% oxygen. When used in high concentration it is suitable for anaesthesia. It has no side effects.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="responsibilities-of-the-midwife">Responsibilities of the Midwife<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#responsibilities-of-the-midwife" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The main responsibilities of the midwife include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Preparing equipment and ensuring it is in good working order</li>
<li>Staying with the patient so as to instruct her on how to use the inhalation apparatus</li>
<li>The midwife should know how the apparatus is used</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="obstetric-operations">Obstetric Operations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#obstetric-operations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>You will now study obstetric operations. The easiest and most important operation is the episiotomy. This is a technique each midwife should master while in the labour ward. This competence is achieved through observing an experienced midwife conducting the procedure. It is an aseptic procedure.</p>
<p>Episiotomy is invasion through the perineal tissues, which is designed to enlarge the vulva outlet during delivery.</p>
<p><strong>Remember:</strong></p>
<p><strong>Give an episiotomy only when indicated.</strong></p>
<p>The main indications of an episiotomy are:</p>
<ul>
<li>Rigid perineum, mostly in primigravidae</li>
<li>Poor maternal effort or maternal distress in second stage</li>
<li>In case of foetal distress in second stage to hasten delivery</li>
<li>When the perineum threatens to tear, for example, in persistent occipito posterior</li>
<li>Prior to assisted delivery such as in low forceps or vacuum delivery</li>
<li>Preeclamptic mother</li>
<li>In mothers who have medical conditions such as cardiac disease or diabetes mellitus</li>
<li>In premature labour to minimise the risks of intracranial injury to the baby</li>
<li>In case the mother has had previous third degree tears which had been repaired</li>
<li>In malpresentation like breech delivery to prevent risks of intracranial injury to the baby</li>
</ul>
<p>There are several types of episiotomy incisions.</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="mediolateral-episiotomy">Mediolateral Episiotomy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mediolateral-episiotomy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>This is the most commonly performed episiotomy due to its safety record. However, it is difficult to repair. It begins at the centre of the fourchette, directed posteriorly and laterally the incision is not more than 3cm at 45Â° to the midline. Move towards a point midway between ischio-tuberosity and the anus. This is to avoid damaging the anal sphincter and the Bartholin's glands.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260112-6cccb92a.jpeg" alt="img-23.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="median-episiotomy">Median Episiotomy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#median-episiotomy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>This begins at the fourchette, is directed posteriorly for approximately 2.5cms and stops just before the anal sphincter. It follows the insertion of perennial muscles and has minimal bleeding due to few blood vessels in this area. It is easy to repair, less painful and rarely causes dyspareunia. However there is the danger of the incision extending to the anal sphincter.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260112-592fd3a2.jpeg" alt="img-24.jpeg">
J Shaped Episiotomy</p>
<p>The incision begins at the centre of the fourchette, is directed posterior for about 2cm and then it is extended latero-posteriorly to avoid damage to the anal sphincter. Suturing of this episiotomy is very difficult.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260112-a8f4913e.jpeg" alt="img-25.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="lateral">Lateral<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#lateral" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Not used now. Unlike in all the other types, the incision does not begin at the centre of the fouchette but on the side of the vaginal opening. The incision may extend leading to a severe vaginal tear and excessive bleeding.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260112-6e107d70.jpeg" alt="img-26.jpeg"></p>
<p>Remember: Episiotomy can comfortably be given without local anaesthesia at the height of a contraction. The first and the second types are more preferred.</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 191 of 317
Bishop's Computers</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="performing-an-episiotomy">Performing an Episiotomy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#performing-an-episiotomy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The timing of the incision is very important. It is best timed when the presenting part is directly applied to the perineum. If the episiotomy is performed too early, it exposes the mother to a lot of bleeding. If performed too late, there will not be enough time to infiltrate the local anaesthesia. A tear may already have developed before the midwife gives an episiotomy.</p>
<p>The main requirement for the procedure is a trolley with:</p>
<ul>
<li>Suture pack</li>
<li>10mls syringes and needles
Lignocaine (0.5% 10ml or 1% 5mls)</li>
<li>Chromic catgut</li>
<li>Needle holder</li>
<li>Suturing scissors</li>
<li>Artery forceps</li>
<li>Toothed dissecting forceps.</li>
<li>Mayo scissors</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260112-a3f381ed.jpeg" alt="img-27.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="procedure">Procedure<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#procedure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>When the head reaches the pelvic floor, two fingers of the left hand are inserted between the perineum and the foetal head. Lignocaine, 0.5%, is infiltrated into the area where the incision has to be made. Using the right hand, the midwife places the tip of the opened scissors and makes an incision at the height of a contraction.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260112-93dd00b2.jpeg" alt="img-28.jpeg">
Infiltrating the Perineum</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260112-86b5e7d5.jpeg" alt="img-29.jpeg">
Performing an Episiotomy</p>
<p>Delivery of the head should follow immediately and it should be controlled to avoid extension of the episiotomy. If there is delay before the head emerges, apply pressure at the episiotomy site between contractions to minimise bleeding. Use aseptic techniques.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="the-method-used-and-the-toxic-signs-of-local-anaesthesia">The Method Used and the Toxic Signs of Local Anaesthesia<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-method-used-and-the-toxic-signs-of-local-anaesthesia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The following method should be used:</p>
<ul>
<li>Direct your needle 4.5cm beneath the skin of the proposed site of injection</li>
<li>Ensure the needle is not in the blood vessel by drawing back the piston</li>
<li>If you withdraw blood, redirect the needle</li>
<li>Inject the lignocaine as you withdraw the needle</li>
</ul>
<p>Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers</p>
<ul>
<li>Distribute the anaesthesia by changing direction of the needle to two or more areas on the proposed injection site</li>
</ul>
<p>The following are toxic signs of local anaesthesia that you should be aware of:</p>
<ul>
<li>Drowsiness</li>
<li>Twitching of the face/lips</li>
<li>Tingling in the area of the mouth</li>
<li>Convulsion</li>
<li>Circulatory collapse</li>
<li>Respiratory collapse</li>
</ul>
<p>If the above signs are noted, call for medical help (anaesthetist) and resuscitate.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="repair-of-the-episiotomy">Repair of the Episiotomy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#repair-of-the-episiotomy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The episiotomy should be repaired as soon as possible (immediately after the third stage) before oedema sets in and while tissues are still anaesthetised. You will need a good source of direct light. The patient is placed in the lithotomy position. The midwife should be seated comfortably during the procedure.</p>
<p>An aseptic technique must be maintained throughout the procedure. The vagina and the episiotomy site are cleaned with antiseptic lotion and the midwife should have a sterile gown and gloves on. Sterile gauze is inserted into the vagina to absorb blood and keep the operation site dry. Absorbable sutures are used. The repair begins at the apex of the vaginal wound. A continuous or interrupted stitch is used, started from the apex to the fourchette bringing the two edges of the wound together. The perineal muscles are then sutured and finally the skin is sutured.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260112-bdb41634.jpeg" alt="img-30.jpeg"></p>
<p>The stitches should just be firm enough. If they are too loose, they may cause oedema and if they are too tight, the mother will be very uncomfortable. After suturing, remove the pack from the vagina and note on the mother's card that the pack has been removed. Insert the little finger into the anal orifice to make sure the two orifices have not been stitched together and the vaginal orifice is still patent.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260112-909d8d18.jpeg" alt="img-31.jpeg">
The repair from the apex of the vagina</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260112-6daa570c.jpeg" alt="img-32.jpeg">
The fascia and muscle of perineum are repaired with three or four interrupted sutures</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260112-aeea79f5.jpeg" alt="img-33.jpeg">
Skin suture</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="care-of-the-episiotomy">Care of the Episiotomy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#care-of-the-episiotomy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Advise the mother on how to take care of the episiotomy site.</p>
<p>This includes:</p>
<ul>
<li>Four hourly seat baths</li>
<li>Change the perineal pad whenever it is soiled</li>
<li>Avoid coitus until the episiotomy wound is healed</li>
<li>Take a balanced diet to promote healing</li>
<li>Maintain good hygiene</li>
<li>Avoid constipation by taking plenty of fluids and roughage, constipation would cause stretching of the sutures during defecation</li>
</ul>
<p>Possible complications to be on the look out for include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Infections leading to broken episiotomy</li>
<li>Haematoma formation at the site of the episiotomy haemorrhage</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="vacuum-extraction-ventouse-delivery">Vacuum Extraction (Ventouse) Delivery<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#vacuum-extraction-ventouse-delivery" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Younge invented the basic idea for the vacuum extractor in 1706 when he used a glass suction cup. In 1849, Simpson designed the instrument, but at the time it was hardly used. In 1774 Mostron introduced the modern vacuum extractor. There are opinions about the value in assisting delivery by this method and it is rarely used these days. However, it is still useful in remote areas.</p>
<p>Indications for vacuum delivery:</p>
<ul>
<li>Mild foetal distress</li>
<li>Delay in second stage of labour</li>
<li>Malposition; occipital lateral and occipital posterior positions</li>
<li>Maternal exhaustion</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="the-procedure">The Procedure<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-procedure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The following steps should be followed when conducting this procedure:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Reassure the mother and explain the necessity of this procedure</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The paediatrician should be present</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Explain to the mother that the baby will have chignon (an area of oedema and bruising where the cup is applied) but this will disappear after some hours</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Equipment as for normal delivery with the addition of vacuum equipment</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The mother should be placed in the lithotomy position</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The doctor should assemble the cup and tubing</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The nurse attaches the distal end to the suction</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The doctor should then swab and prepare the mother</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Catheterisation is done to empty the bladder</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The perineum should be infiltrated with 1% lignocaine</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The cup should be dipped in sterile water then introduced sideways into the vagina by pressing backwards against the perineum</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>It is placed on the scalp as near as possible to the posterior fontanelle</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Care should be taken not to trap the cervix or the vaginal wall under the cup</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>While the doctor holds the cup in the correct position:</p>
<ul>
<li>The pressure causes an artificial caput succedaneum or chignon, when vacuum reaches 0.8kg/cm the cup is completely filled with scalp</li>
<li>Traction on the handle should be made as nearly vertically to the cup as possible as oblique direction may pull the cup off</li>
<li>The nurse uses the hand pump to create vacuum gradually</li>
<li>Increase negative pressure by 0.2kg/cm at one minute interval until 0.8kg/cm is attained</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260112-b982f00f.jpeg" alt="img-34.jpeg"></p>
<p>he procedure continues as follows:</p>
<ul>
<li>Intermittent traction is applied with uterine contraction</li>
</ul>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 194 of 317
Bishop's Computers</p>
<ul>
<li>Direction of pull changes as the head descends through the birth canal</li>
<li>When crowning takes place episiotomy is performed if necessary</li>
<li>The use of ventouse should be reconsidered if there is no obvious descent after three to four contractions</li>
<li>To prevent damage to the scalp, the vacuum is reduced as slowly as it was created after delivery of the head by opening the screw release valve</li>
<li>The cup is then detached</li>
<li>Should the cup detach itself, it is probably due to pulling in the wrong direction or using too much force</li>
<li>A vacuum should be created again and if the chignon is large, then another area on the scalp is used</li>
</ul>
<p>Remember:
Never use the cup actively to rotate the baby's head during the procedure. Do not continue this procedure for more than 30 minutes.</p>
<p>What complications should you watch out for during and after the procedure?
â˜ Failure of the procedure
â˜ Trauma to the foetal scalp
â˜ Chignon, that is, oedema and bruising where the cup had been applied, which can occasionally get infected
â˜ Some babies develop cephalohaematoma
â˜ Intracranial haemorrhage
â˜ Necrosis of the scalp
â˜ Aponeurotic haematoma
â˜ These complications occur mainly due to some degree of disproportion where the cup has been applied for long period and forceful traction used</p>
<p>Forceps Delivery</p>
<p>This procedure is performed by a forceps which is an instrument that has two parts that cross each other like scissors and lock at the intersection. The lock may be of sliding type or of screw type. Each part consists of a handle, a lock, a shank and a blade. The blade is joined to the handle by a shank. The blade has two curves, cephalic curve to fit the head, and pelvic curve that correspond with the curved axis of the pelvis. The length of the handles differ, so do the types of handles.</p>
<p>There are several types of forceps including Kielland's, Simpson's, Wrigley's, Neville-Barne's, Haig-Fwerguson's, Milne-Murray and Diper forceps among others.</p>
<p>Types of Forceps Delivery</p>
<p>Low Forceps</p>
<p>Today the majority of forceps delivery is carried out when the foetal head is on the perineal floor whereby the internal rotation may have already occurred. This is called outlet forceps or low forceps delivery.</p>
<p>Mid Forceps</p>
<p>This is when the head is higher in the pelvis but engaged and the greater diameter has passed the inlet. This is known as mid forceps.</p>
<p>High Forceps</p>
<p>If the head is not engaged, the procedure is termed high forceps. This is an extremely difficult and dangerous operation. A caesarean section is usually preferred to mid/high forceps.</p>
<p>What conditions have to be present for a forceps delivery?</p>
<p>Conditions considered for forceps delivery include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Presentation must be suitable</li>
<li>Head has to be engaged</li>
<li>The pelvic outlet needs to be adequate</li>
<li>Good uterine contraction</li>
<li>Membranes should be ruptured</li>
<li>Bladder must be empty</li>
</ul>
<p>What steps should be taken before the application of forceps?</p>
<p>The following steps should be taken before the application of forceps:</p>
<ul>
<li>Reassure the mother and explain the procedure.</li>
<li>Obtain consent from the mother.</li>
<li>Some form of analgesia is given. Pundental or epidural block is preferred to general anaesthesia.</li>
<li>Ensure requirements for catheterisation, episiotomy and perineal sutures are at hand.</li>
<li>Resuscitation trolley must be ready.</li>
<li>Delivery trolley should be ready as for spontaneous delivery.</li>
</ul>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<ul>
<li>The specific type of forceps as per doctor's requirement.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="procedure">Procedure<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#procedure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The following procedure should be followed:</p>
<ul>
<li>The mother is given analgesia and placed in the lithotomy position.</li>
<li>The vulva is swabbed and draped.</li>
<li>Catheterisation is done.</li>
<li>The physician checks the exact position of the foetal head by vaginal examination.</li>
<li>The fingers of the right hand are passed in the vagina.</li>
<li>The left blade is applied first and held by the left hand between the fingers and thumbs of the left hand.</li>
<li>The blade is then passed between the head and the palm or surface of the right fingers. The handle is carried backwards towards the middle well over the mother's abdomen to the right side almost parallel with her right inguinal ligament.</li>
<li>The above position of the blade will ensure the instrument follows the directions of both the pelvic and cephalic curve.</li>
<li>After ascertaining it lies in the correct position next to the head, the fingers of the right hand are withdrawn.</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260112-17f1734f.jpeg" alt="img-35.jpeg"></p>
<p>The same procedure is carried out on the right side. The external visible portion will be above the blade.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="positioning-the-forceps">Positioning the Forceps<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#positioning-the-forceps" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The shanks are pressed backwards against the perineum and the handle should lock and lie in a horizontal position. If the handle does not lock, the blades should be removed and the position of the head re-examined.</p>
<p>The ordinary curved forceps, if correctly applied on the foetal head, results in the fenestrate, 'window' of the blade lying over the pariental eminence. The fingers of the right hand resting on the cheek, guide the tip of the blade.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260112-4c94fb56.jpeg" alt="img-36.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-delivery-procedure">The Delivery Procedure<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-delivery-procedure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Before applying traction, ascertain that the cervix is not nipped between the foetal head and the forceps blade. Traction is applied during contractions, which should not exceed 15 seconds. Encourage the mother to push with every contraction. The lock on the handle should be loosened between contractions to reduce the skull pressure. Continuously monitor the foetal heart. The direction of pull is altered as the head descends to follow the curve of birth canal. If the head is mid cavity the direction of the pull is outwards.</p>
<p>The blades lie in submento vertical while the biparietal diameter is grasped. As the head descends, the handles are gradually raised to about <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msup><mn>45</mn><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">âˆ˜</mo></msup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">45^{\circ}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6741em;"></span><span class="mord">4</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord">5</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.6741em;"><span style="top: -3.063em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight">âˆ˜</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> above the horizontal, and then episiotomy is performed through a stretched perineum. The head is then gently guided through the vulva until crowning takes place. The handles of the forceps should be in vertical position. After the head is properly crowned and ready for extension, the forceps are removed. The face is delivered by manual extension of the head.</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260112-128478f6.jpeg" alt="img-37.jpeg"></p>
<p>You should note that the forceps delivery poses several dangers both to the mother and baby.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="do-you-know-what-these-are">Do you know what these are?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#do-you-know-what-these-are" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In the case of the mother dangers arise from:</p>
<ul>
<li>Anaesthesia</li>
<li>Laceration of cervix, vagina or perineum</li>
<li>Postpartum haemorrhage</li>
<li>Puerperium infection</li>
</ul>
<p>In the case of the baby, danger may arise as a result of:</p>
<ul>
<li>Intra cranial haemorrhage</li>
<li>Facial palsy</li>
<li>Cephalohaematoma</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="piper-forceps-for-breech-delivery-of">Piper Forceps for Breech Delivery of<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#piper-forceps-for-breech-delivery-of" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="aftercoming-head">Aftercoming Head<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#aftercoming-head" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The Piper forceps is used electively as a substitute in case of failure of Mauriceau-Smellie-Veit manoeuvre for delivery of the foetal head. The forceps are applied after delivery of the shoulder while the head is in the pelvis. The body and the arms are suspended with a towel. The left blade is introduced in an upward direction along the foetal head. The same is done to apply the right forceps.</p>
<p>The forceps are locked in place and the position of the head is confirmed by palpation. An episiotomy is performed in case it had not been done earlier. Traction is applied until the chin the mouth and nose emerge over the perineum. The forceps are removed and the mother is instructed to pant so that the head is delivered slowly.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="caesarean-section">Caesarean Section<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#caesarean-section" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Caesarian section is the delivery of the foetus through an incision made on the abdominal wall and uterus. It is considered a major abdominal surgery. The diminished danger of caesarean section has made it widely used and even abused at times.</p>
