<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="indications">Indications<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#indications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The following are indications of caesarean section:</p>
<ul>
<li>Maternal or foetal distress during labour</li>
<li>Pelvic tumour</li>
<li>Diabetes mellitus</li>
<li>Cephalopelvic disproportion</li>
<li>Severe high blood pressure</li>
<li>Abnormal uterine action</li>
<li>Haemolytic diseases</li>
<li>Failed induction</li>
<li>Placenta previa</li>
<li>Antepartum haemorrhage</li>
<li>Gross disproportions</li>
<li>Cervical or vaginal stenosis</li>
<li>Fault in birth canal</li>
<li>Double uterus</li>
<li>Impacted mentoposterior</li>
<li>Foetal malpresentation</li>
<li>Shoulder presentation</li>
<li>Breech presentation</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="types-of-caesarean-section">Types of Caesarean Section<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-caesarean-section" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>You should note that the forceps delivery poses several dangers both to the mother and baby.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="what-are-the-different-types-of-caesarean-section-called">What are the different types of caesarean section called?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-are-the-different-types-of-caesarean-section-called" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>â˜ Lower segment section, which is the operation of choice
â˜ Classical section
â˜ Extraperitonial caesarean section
â˜ Caesarean hysterectomy</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="can-you-think-why-a-lower-segment-section-procedure-would-be-the-operation-of-choice">Can you think why a lower segment section procedure would be the operation of choice?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#can-you-think-why-a-lower-segment-section-procedure-would-be-the-operation-of-choice" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The main advantages of lower segment section are:</p>
<ul>
<li>Blood loss is minimal</li>
<li>Incision is easy to repair</li>
</ul>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 197 of 317
Bishop's Computers</p>
<ul>
<li>The risk of rupture during labour is lessened as the lower uterine segment has less uterine activity</li>
<li>The operation is associated with lower incidence of postoperative infection</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="lower-segment-caesarean-section">Lower Segment Caesarean Section<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#lower-segment-caesarean-section" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The following steps make up the procedure to be followed in the lower segment section:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>The bladder is emptied by catheterisation.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Intravenous glucose saline is started (kept ready).</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The operation table is tilted to prevent compression of inferior vena cava.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>A transverse or vertical incision is made out of the lower subumbilical to open the peritoneal cavity.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>At the end of the wound a wide retractor is inserted.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>To push the bladder off from the lower segment, the uterovesical pouch is divided transversely for about 10cm.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>A transverse incision about 2cm long is made in the middle of the lower segment.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Deepen until the membranes bulge.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>If possible the amnion sack should be kept intact.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The incision is extended to 10cm by exerting traction using two index fingers at the incision.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The membranes are ruptured.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The hand is then slipped beside the head and the first blade of Wringley's forceps is applied, and the other follows.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>As the head is delivered gently with the forceps, the anaesthetist injects ten units of syntocinon intravenously.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The shoulders are eased out carefully to avoid lateral splitting of the uterine wound.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The delivered foetus is held upside down, the air passage cleared by suctioning.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The cord is clamped and cut and the baby is handed to the assistant for further care.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The placenta separates immediately and is delivered through the wound.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The uterine incision is sutured with two layers with catgut or dexon.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Any blood, liquor, vernix is removed from the peritoneal cavity and the wound closed.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="classical-caesarean-section">Classical Caesarean Section<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#classical-caesarean-section" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The incision is made directly into the wall of the body of the uterus. The procedure is rarely performed, its indications are:</p>
<ul>
<li>Gestation of less than 32 weeks (i.e before the lower segment has formed)</li>
<li>Placenta previa which is anteriorly situated</li>
<li>An hour glass contraction (constriction ring)</li>
</ul>
<p>It is always performed through a midline incision.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="extra-peritoneal-caesarean-section-procedure">Extra Peritoneal Caesarean Section Procedure<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#extra-peritoneal-caesarean-section-procedure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Access to the lower uterine segment is secured by appropriate dissection of tissues around the bladder to by pass the peritoneal cavity and the baby is extracted. As the peritoneal cavity is not disturbed there is no risk of introducing infection from infected liquor or infection from the uterus. This was a popular procedure in the preantibiotic era but is now outdated.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="caesarean-section-hysterectomy">Caesarean Section Hysterectomy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#caesarean-section-hysterectomy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is also known as Porro's Operation. The removal of the uterus follows after caesarean section, due to other conditions of the uterus; such as placenta accreta, multiple fibroid tumours of the uterus and so on. On rare occasions and in conjunction with other gynaecological disorders this operation may be used for sterilisation purposes.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="elective-caesarean-section">Elective Caesarean Section<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#elective-caesarean-section" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The decision to deliver by caesarean section is made during pregnancy before the onset of labour. Some reasons for this decision are absolute while others depend on combination of factors and the opinion of the obstetrician.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="emergency-caesarean-section">Emergency Caesarean Section<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#emergency-caesarean-section" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This operation is performed when adverse conditions develop during labour. The psychological preparation of the mother for the operation is of paramount importance. You should be prepared to deal with the different</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>feelings of different mothers. An opportunity should be given to mothers to explore and express their feelings, be they fear, disappointment or frustration. This can be done in a group or individual counselling setting, where uncertainties and misunderstandings can be clarified. The nurse can be of great help acting as a mediator, fostering acceptance and sense of readiness to both the apprehensive mother and her partner</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="pre-operative-care-for-elective">Pre-Operative Care For Elective<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pre-operative-care-for-elective" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="caesarean-section">Caesarean Section<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#caesarean-section" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The following are characteristic of pre-operative care during an elective caesarean section:</p>
<ul>
<li>The doctor explains the procedure to the mother and her partner and consent is obtained.</li>
<li>Physical examination is carried out to make sure the mother is fit for general anaesthesia</li>
<li>Blood for haemoglobin, cross match and two pints of blood are kept ready.</li>
<li>Mother is admitted and not fed overnight. Sodium amytal (200mg) is given to ensure a good night's sleep.</li>
<li>The abdomen is cleaned in the morning.</li>
<li>A bath is taken in the morning.</li>
<li>A retention catheter is inserted to ensure an empty bladder through the operation.</li>
<li>An intravenous infusion is started as per prescription.</li>
<li>Valuables are kept safely.</li>
<li>Nail polish, dentures, glasses or contact lenses are removed.</li>
<li>Theatre gown, leggings and scarf are put on the mother.</li>
<li>Pre-operative medication is usually administered half an hour before the operation (1m atropine and analgesic).</li>
<li>Foetal heart, foetal position, and presentation are determined.</li>
<li>Maternal observations are recorded: pulse, respiration, blood pressure and temperature.</li>
<li>A urinalysis is carried out for albumin sugar.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="unanticipated-caesarean-section">Unanticipated Caesarean Section<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#unanticipated-caesarean-section" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In such a situation, the mother's anxiety will be high. Reassure the mother and explain the</p>
<p>reasons for surgery. The procedure is the same as outlined for elective Caesarean but if food has been consumed, gastric lavage should be performed.</p>
<p><strong>Remember: In some countries midwives are trained to perform caesarean sections.</strong></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="post-operative-care">Post Operative Care<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#post-operative-care" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is the same care given to any woman who has undergone a major abdominal operation. For more details, refer to module one, unit four.</p>
<p>Additional care steps are also recommended. The mother should breast feed as soon as her condition permits. If for any reason she cannot breast feed, the breast should manually be expressed from the third day to prevent engorgement of the breasts. Four hourly vulva swabbing should be taken if the patient is confined to bed.</p>
<p>Remember that maternal mortality is four times greater than in normal labour. Elective sections usually have lower mortality rates but emergency cases are usually at high risk, especially due to the use of anaesthesia. Mothers who were in labour for a prolonged period are especially at risk of serious infection; so prophylactic antibiotics should always be used. A ruptured uterus is more rare here than in the lower segment section. All mothers with a caesarean section scar should be delivered in the hospital under vigilant observation.</p>
<p>The foetus is also at risk, given that respiratory problems may occur due to the anaesthesia. Intracranial damage may occur as a result of improper care during the delivery of the foetal head, which has to be brought up from the pelvis or through the small uterine incision.</p>
<p>Obstetric emergencies may occur suddenly or may be due to poor management or negligence on the part of the skilled medical personnel. You should always be vigilant in your observations in an effort to avoid such emergencies. When they do happen, you should be ready to respond in order to save lives and reduce morbidity and mortality.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="obstetric-emergencies">Obstetric Emergencies<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#obstetric-emergencies" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="obstetric-emergencies">Obstetric Emergencies<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#obstetric-emergencies" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>You will now look at some obstetric emergencies and how you can prevent them and systematically deal with them.</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="vasa-praevia">Vasa Praevia<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#vasa-praevia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>This condition occurs when there is a velamentous insertion and the blood vessel from the cord lies over the os, in front of the presenting part. This endangers the life of the foetus. Vasa praevia can be felt on virginal examination when the membranes are still intact. The condition can be visualised on ultrasound. A speculum examination should be undertaken if this is suspected. When the membranes rupture, the foetal vessel may also rupture. The rupture of vessels should be suspected when there is fresh bleeding after the rupture of the membranes following foetal distress.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management-of-vasa-praevia">Management of Vasa Praevia<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-vasa-praevia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>You should inform the doctor immediately. Take the foetal heartbeat and, if the foetus is alive, administer oxygen and prepare the mother for caesarean section.</p>
<p>A paediatrician should be present at the time of delivery of the baby. The baby's haemoglobin should be estimated and transfused as necessary. There is high mortality associated with this condition.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="presentation-of-the-cord">Presentation of the Cord<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#presentation-of-the-cord" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is a condition where the cord lies in front of the presenting part and the membranes are intact.</p>
<p>Cord prolapse is a term used when the umbilical cord lies in front of the presenting part and the membranes are ruptured.</p>
<p>Occult prolapse describes the condition that occurs when the cord lies alongside, but not in front of, the presenting part.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260112-1eca78d2.jpeg" alt="img-38.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="causes-of-cord-prolapse">Causes of Cord Prolapse<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causes-of-cord-prolapse" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Any condition in which the presenting part does not fit well into the lower uterine segment will permit the umbilical cord to slip down in front of the presenting part, for example, malpresentation and malposition, breech presentation, face and brow presentation, shoulder presentation resulting from transverse lie and occipito posterior position.</p>
<p>Malpresentation, polyhydramnious and prematurity are conditions that are more common in multiple pregnancies, all of which can cause cord prolapse.</p>
<ul>
<li>Contracted pelvis: because the membranes may rupture before the head has engaged.</li>
<li>Certain placental and cord conditions like low implantation of the placenta, marginal insertion of the cord and a long cord.</li>
<li>High head: the membranes rupture spontaneously when the foetal head is still high. Also artificial rupture of the membranes is contraindicated in high head.</li>
<li>Prematurity: there is more room between the small foetal head and the maternal pelvis.</li>
<li>Polyhydramnios: the cord is likely to be swept down in a gush of liquor when the membranes rupture spontaneously.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="how-would-you-diagnose-cord-presentation-or-cord-prolapse">How would you diagnose cord presentation or cord prolapse?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#how-would-you-diagnose-cord-presentation-or-cord-prolapse" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>During labour cord presentation or prolapse can be diagnosed as follows:</p>
<ul>
<li>On vaginal examination a soft pulsating mass can be felt in front of the presenting part with the membranes intact.</li>
<li>A cord may be felt in the vagina or seen at the vulva either pulsating or not pulsating.</li>
<li>Whenever the membranes rupture a vaginal examination should be done to rule out cord prolapse.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management-of-cord-presentation">Management of Cord Presentation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-cord-presentation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>As soon as you get cord presentation, which is rare, you should remove your fingers, taking care not to rupture the membranes. Explain to</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>the mother the situation at hand. Ask your assistant to inform the doctor and theatre staff to prepare for emergency caesarean section while you prepare the mother for the section. Take the mother to theatre as soon as possible as the membranes may rupture at any minute.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management-of-cord-prolapse">Management of Cord Prolapse<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-cord-prolapse" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>If you diagnose prolapse of the cord while performing a vaginal examination, check for the following factors that determine the method of management. Check whether the pulsation of the cord cervical dilatation is in the first or second stage. Determine the adequacy of the pelvis. If the cord is pulsating you must act very fast in order to save the baby.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="pulsating-cord-with-mother-in-first-stage">Pulsating Cord with Mother in First Stage<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pulsating-cord-with-mother-in-first-stage" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Explain to the mother the situation at hand while you push up the presenting part so as not to compress the cord. If the cord is outside the vagina, gently replace it in the vagina to prevent spasm and keep warm. Instruct your assistant to inform the obstetrician and the theatre staff, and keep the mother in knee chest position without removing your fingers. Continue elevating the presenting part until the patient is in theatre.</p>
<p>Your assistant should give the mother oxygen by facemask while someone else draws blood for grouping and cross matching. At this point you should commence an intravenous line and keep the vein open. The mother should be asked</p>
<p>when she last had a meal and gastric aspiration should be commenced if necessary.</p>
<p>Once consent has been taken, the mother should be rushed to the theatre as soon as possible. If the cervical os is fully dilated and the pelvis is adequate, you should encourage the mother to push. Tell the assistant to inform the doctor and prepare for vacuum extraction. Continue encouraging the mother to push and give a generous episiotomy to hasten the delivery of the baby. Should the doctor arrive before the baby is out, he may perform vacuum extraction. If there is malpresentation, the patient should be quickly prepared for caesarean section as per steps above.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="if-the-cord-is-not-pulsating">If the Cord is not Pulsating<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#if-the-cord-is-not-pulsating" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The procedure to be followed varies from institution to institution. In some institutions you may be able to personally inform the patient of the situation. Otherwise, you may have to wait until the doctor comes to tell the patient about her dead foetus. If the patient is in first stage of labour and the pelvis is adequate, let nature take its course and deliver a fresh stillbirth. If the patient is in the second stage, she is encouraged to push and she will deliver a stillbirth. In case there is a contracted pelvis, a caesarean section should be performed in spite of the death of the foetus.</p>
